Yes. From here I would attack in **two live directions**, and I would stop spending time on a few lanes that now look exhausted.

The clearest conclusion from the current draft state is that the **nonmixed repeated-source / route-2 package is exhausted inside its present variables**. The draft’s own updated frontier is: one-sign-change chambers are sterile; entry into the adjacent-two-odd-zero chamber does not create the first rooted point; fixed anchor-sign continuation does not allow crossing; odd-anchor passage does not reset the defect; the first dangerous post-anchor chamber is already formally realizable in the planar normalized model; and, more strongly, the whole current source package ((\Psi_a,\mathfrak D,\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}},D_{f_a})) is still universal under normalization. So the next theorem cannot be “one more sign argument” inside that same package. It has to use the **first genuinely non-universal source-coupled ingredient**, something not already absorbed by the planar normalized ((\mathcal Z,\mathcal R,D_a)) model. The draft itself now identifies that as the real dividing line.

So the first serious attack is:

**Attack A: identify the first non-universal source-coupled invariant.**
A good test is immediate: can the candidate still be realized in the universal normalized lift
[
c=1,\qquad v_5=t,\qquad \lambda=t^2,\qquad u_5''=2\mathcal Z?
]
If yes, it will not close route 2. If no, then it is finally using RH-specific source structure. The most natural candidates named in the current notes are **quotient-septic / mixed-level data**, especially something provenance-sensitive rather than just arbitrary quotient-septic geometry; the notes explicitly flag ([A_7^{\mathfrak f}]) and (\Delta_7) as the first canonical places to look. Just as importantly, the notes also warn that arbitrary canonical quotient-septic geometry is still too free, so the theorem you want is not “a new quotient-septic object exists,” but “some quotient-septic / mixed object obeys an RH-specific relation that fails in the universal model.”

The second live direction is on the mixed residual side.

The transcript now points much more sharply to the **exact fixed-shear (K_v=0) quotient-diagonal / involutive residue** as the place where a new law might actually bite. The suggested next theorem there is an **involution descent theorem**: show that the relevant highest-new scalar on the exact fixed-shear slice is involution-even, hence descends to the quotient coordinate (u=t^2), and then prove that in that quotient variable the residual branch cannot support a new overlap without diagonal collapse or one of the already-classified quartic–sextic models. This is a much sharper target than the abandoned global gap-function story. It uses the exact new structure the two-point work produced and attacks the one place the notes still regard as genuinely mixed and live.

So the second serious attack is:

**Attack B: prove involution descent / quotient-visible transport on the exact fixed-shear (K_v=0) slice.**
Concretely, try to prove that the controlling residual scalar (X(t)) is even under (t\mapsto -t), so
[
X(t)=\widetilde X(t^2),
]
or else that the differential defect rank drops under the involution quotient. If you get that, the remaining residual overlap problem is no longer a free two-sided germ in (t), but a much more rigid quotient germ in (u=t^2). That is precisely the kind of structural compression that the current draft does **not** yet have, and it is the sharpest live target on the quotient/mixed side.

What I would **not** attack further:

* I would not keep pushing the current **route-2 scalar/discriminant package** for another internal contradiction. The notes are explicit that the first dangerous post-anchor chamber is already formally compatible with the rooted equations and fold data, and that the present source package is universal under normalization. That means more work with the same quartet is very unlikely to close anything.
* I would not revive the claim that the **quotient-cusp lane is already globally closed by a monotone gap function**. Those notes are exactly the overclaim you already decided not to import. At best, that line is still an unproved plan; at worst, it distracts from the sharper involutive/quotient-diagonal target.

So my prioritized recommendation is:

First, attack the **non-universal source-coupled ingredient** question, with an explicit “fails in the universal model or not?” test. Second, in parallel, attack the **involution descent theorem on the exact fixed-shear (K_v=0) slice**. If either one lands, it gives a genuinely new theorem. If both stall, then the right conclusion is not “push harder on route 2,” but “the current paper has reached the ceiling of its present source package.”

The cleanest next thing I can do is turn those two attacks into draft-ready theorem statements and a proof agenda for each.

_Thought for 5m 38s_

I think Attack B does go through in a stronger form than the current draft states.

The real gain is not just that the scalar
\[
Q(t)=\frac{J_{u_5}(t)}{J_\lambda(t)}
\]
is even on the exact fixed-shear involutive branch. It is that the entire **parity-normalized transport jet** descends to the quotient variable
\[
u=t^2.
\]
And on the first surviving rung \((m,n)=(4,6)\), that descended jet is actually determined by \(Q\) alone.

Here is the clean mathematical picture.

---

Assume we are on the additional exact fixed-shear overlap lane near
\[
a\in\{S=0\}\cap\{K_v=0\},
\]
with involutive parametrization
\[
(h_1,h_2)=(h(t),h(-t)),
\qquad h(0)=a,
\qquad h'(0)\neq 0,
\]
and write as in the draft
\[
Q(t)=\frac{J_{u_5}(t)}{J_\lambda(t)}=\widehat Q(t^2).
\]

The current draft already has this evenness. The next step is to push it from one scalar to the whole transport jet.

Define, for each \(k\ge 0\),
\[
\Theta_k(t):=t^{-(k\bmod 2)}\,Q^{(k)}(t).
\]
So explicitly,
\[
\Theta_0=Q,\qquad
\Theta_1=t^{-1}Q',\qquad
\Theta_2=Q'',\qquad
\Theta_3=t^{-1}Q''',\ \dots
\]

Then:

\[
\boxed{\Theta_k(-t)=\Theta_k(t)\ \text{ for every }k\ge 0.}
\]

The proof is very simple. Since \(Q\) is even, \(Q^{(k)}\) has parity \(k\): even for \(k\) even, odd for \(k\) odd. Every odd analytic germ is divisible by \(t\). Hence each \(\Theta_k\) is even analytic. Therefore there are unique analytic germs
\[
\widetilde\Theta_k(u)
\]
such that
\[
\Theta_k(t)=\widetilde\Theta_k(t^2).
\]

So the whole normalized transport jet factors through the quotient:
\[
t\longmapsto \bigl(\Theta_0(t),\Theta_1(t),\dots,\Theta_N(t)\bigr)
\]
descends to
\[
u\longmapsto \bigl(\widetilde\Theta_0(u),\widetilde\Theta_1(u),\dots,\widetilde\Theta_N(u)\bigr).
\]

That already gives the “differential defect rank drop” version of Attack B: after quotienting by the involution, the local transport state is not a two-sided \(t\)-germ anymore. It is a one-parameter \(u\)-germ.

A particularly canonical choice is
\[
X(t):=\frac{Q'(t)}{t}
=
\frac{\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}(t)}{t\,J_\lambda(t)^2}.
\]
Then
\[
X(t)=2\,\widehat{\mathcal D}(t^2),
\qquad
\widehat{\mathcal D}(u)=\widehat Q'(u),
\]
so this “controlling residual scalar” is automatically even. That is the cleanest direct realization of the target suggested in Attack B.

You can also write the first few descended jet coordinates explicitly:
\[
t^{-1}Q'(t)=2\widehat Q'(u),
\]
\[
Q''(t)=2\widehat Q'(u)+4u\,\widehat Q''(u),
\]
\[
t^{-1}Q'''(t)=12\widehat Q''(u)+8u\,\widehat Q'''(u),
\]
and so on. So the quotient jet algebra is closed.

That gives a stronger general statement:

If \(X(t)\) is any analytic scalar obtained from finitely many of the normalized jet coordinates
\[
\Theta_0(t),\dots,\Theta_N(t)
\]
by an analytic formula, then
\[
X(t)=\widetilde X(t^2)
\]
for a unique analytic quotient germ \(\widetilde X(u)\). In other words, **every finite transport-jet scalar is quotient-visible**.

This is exactly the right form of “no hidden odd reset” at the local level: there is no extra local two-sheet state hiding in higher transport derivatives. Any such finite-order state already lives on the quotient branch.

Now the first rung becomes even sharper.

In the quartic-sextic case
\[
(m,n)=(4,6),
\]
the draft already gives
\[
(r,e)=(2,0),
\qquad
\widehat Q'(0)=\widehat{\mathcal D}(0)\neq 0.
\]
Hence \(\widehat Q\) is a local analytic coordinate in \(u\). Therefore each descended jet coordinate is not merely a function of \(u\); it is an analytic function of \(Q\) itself:
\[
\widetilde\Theta_k(u)=F_k(\widehat Q(u)),
\]
so
\[
\Theta_k(t)=F_k(Q(t)).
\]

That is the strongest local compression I can justify from the present draft:

\[
\boxed{\text{On the quartic-sextic rung, every local finite transport-jet scalar is an analytic function of }Q\text{ alone.}}
\]

So on that first surviving residual rung, the local quotient transport state has rank \(1\) in the strongest possible sense. There is no room for a second independent local hidden state.

What this does and does not buy you:

It does buy you a real structural theorem. The exact fixed-shear \(K_v=0\) corner is no longer merely “organized by one scalar” pointwise; the whole parity-normalized finite transport jet descends to the quotient, and on the first rung it is completely controlled by \(Q\).

It does not yet prove global no-reentry. A global reset could still occur by revisiting a value later along the \(u\)-curve. What is excluded is a specifically local involutive two-sided hidden reset mechanism.

So the clean handback is:

The best version of Attack B is a **transport-jet involution descent theorem**. It proves that on the exact fixed-shear corner, every parity-normalized finite transport jet scalar is quotient-visible, and in the quartic-sextic case every such scalar is locally a function of \(Q\) alone. That sharpens the draft’s current quotient-scalar reduction into a full local quotient-visibility theorem.

The remaining gap is now very specific: you still need either

1. a theorem that the actual corrected overlap defects \(E_{12}^{(3)},E_{12}^{(5)}\) on that corner are transport-jet functionals of this descended package, or

2. a global one-variable no-reentry theorem on the quotient branch.

If you want, the next step is for me to turn this into exact draft-ready theorem/proposition/corollary insertions keyed to the existing \(K_v=0\) quotient-transport section.

## Assistant (2026-04-21 16:35:23)

_Thought for 2m 58s_

I pushed the attack one step further, and the sharpest thing I can justify is this:

on the exact fixed-shear residual corner
\[
\{S=0\}\cap\{K_v=0\},
\]
the draft’s quotient-scalar reduction can be upgraded to a **finite transport-state quotient descent theorem**, and on the quartic–sextic rung this becomes a **no finite-order hidden reset theorem**.

That is stronger than the current draft, and it isolates the exact remaining gap.

---

## 1. Full finite transport-jet descent

You already have on the involutive branch
\[
(h_1,h_2)=(h(t),h(-t)),
\qquad
Q(t):=\frac{J_{u_5}(t)}{J_\lambda(t)}=\widehat Q(t^2).
\]

Define the parity-normalized transport jets
\[
\Theta_k(t):=t^{-(k\bmod 2)}Q^{(k)}(t),\qquad k\ge 0.
\]
So
\[
\Theta_0=Q,\qquad
\Theta_1=t^{-1}Q',\qquad
\Theta_2=Q'',\qquad
\Theta_3=t^{-1}Q''',\dots
\]

Because \(Q\) is even, each \(\Theta_k\) is even analytic, hence
\[
\Theta_k(t)=\widetilde\Theta_k(t^2)
\]
for a unique analytic quotient germ \(\widetilde\Theta_k(u)\).

So the entire finite transport jet
\[
\Theta^{\le N}(t):=(\Theta_0(t),\dots,\Theta_N(t))
\]
descends to the quotient variable \(u=t^2\):
\[
\Theta^{\le N}(t)=\widetilde\Theta^{\le N}(t^2).
\]

This is the clean “differential defect rank drop” version of Attack B: locally there is no longer a two-sided \(t\)-state, only a one-parameter quotient state.

A canonical first descended scalar is
\[
X(t):=\frac{Q'(t)}{t}=2\,\widehat Q'(t^2)=2\widehat{\mathcal D}(t^2),
\]
so the proposed “controlling residual scalar” is indeed automatically even.

---

## 2. Quartic–sextic rung: the whole finite transport state is a function of \(Q\)

Now specialize to the first surviving rung
\[
(m,n)=(4,6),
\qquad (r,e)=(2,0).
\]
Then the draft already gives
\[
\widehat Q'(0)=\widehat{\mathcal D}(0)\neq 0.
\]
So \(\widehat Q\) is a local analytic coordinate in \(u\). Therefore every descended jet coordinate is not only a function of \(u\), but an analytic function of \(Q\) itself:
\[
\widetilde\Theta_k(u)=F_k(\widehat Q(u)).
\]
Equivalently,
\[
\Theta_k(t)=F_k(Q(t)).
\]

So on the quartic–sextic rung:

\[
\boxed{\text{every finite parity-normalized transport-jet scalar is an analytic function of }Q\text{ alone}.}
\]

That is the strongest local compression I can see from the present package. The local transport state has rank \(1\).

---

## 3. No finite-order hidden reset theorem

This gives a real new theorem.

Let
\[
\mathcal T_N(t):=(\Theta_0(t),\dots,\Theta_N(t)).
\]
In the quartic–sextic case there exists an analytic map \(\mathbf F_N\) such that
\[
\mathcal T_N(t)=\mathbf F_N(Q(t)).
\]

Hence if for two nearby parameters \(t_1,t_2\),
\[
\mathcal T_N(t_1)=\mathcal T_N(t_2),
\]
then
\[
Q(t_1)=Q(t_2).
\]
Since \(Q(t)=\widehat Q(t^2)\) and \(\widehat Q\) is locally injective in \(u=t^2\),
\[
t_1^2=t_2^2,
\qquad\text{so}\qquad
t_2=\pm t_1.
\]

So:

\[
\boxed{\text{On the quartic–sextic residual corner, no finite transport-jet state admits a third local reset point.}}
\]

The only local duplication is the involution pair \(t\leftrightarrow -t\), which is already known and quotient-trivial.

That is a sharper result than the current “\(Q\) is locally injective in the quotient variable” statement. It says the **entire finite transport package** sees no extra local reset.

---

## 4. The right conditional closure statement

This now gives the exact conditional theorem you want for the actual defects.

Suppose along the residual involutive branch the actual corrected cubic/quintic two-pair defects satisfy
\[
E_{12}^{(3)}(t)=\mathfrak E_3(\Theta^{\le N}(t)),
\qquad
E_{12}^{(5)}(t)=\mathfrak E_5(\Theta^{\le N}(t))
\]
for some analytic functionals \(\mathfrak E_3,\mathfrak E_5\), and suppose they vanish on coincident atoms:
\[
E_{12}^{(3)}(0)=0,\qquad E_{12}^{(5)}(0)=0.
\]

Then, because \(\Theta^{\le N}(t)\) is quotient-visible, both defects are even analytic functions of \(t\). Therefore
\[
E_{12}^{(3)}(t)=O(t^2),
\qquad
E_{12}^{(5)}(t)=O(t^2).
\]
Since
\[
h(t)-h(-t)=2h'(0)t+O(t^3),
\]
this gives
\[
E_{12}^{(3)}=O((h_1-h_2)^2),
\qquad
E_{12}^{(5)}=O((h_1-h_2)^2).
\]
Then your existing defect-scale closeness estimate closes the branch.

So the exact remaining bridge is now extremely precise:

\[
\boxed{\text{Show that the actual corrected defects on the residual corner are finite transport-jet functionals.}}
\]

If that is true, Attack B closes the corner.

---

## 5. What this does and does not prove

What it proves:

- the exact fixed-shear \(K_v=0\) corner has no genuinely two-sided local finite-order transport state;
- on the quartic–sextic rung the full finite transport package is controlled by \(Q\) alone;
- there is no finite-order local hidden reset beyond the involution;
- any actual defect built analytically from that finite transport state is automatically even, and with diagonal vanishing becomes \(O((h_1-h_2)^2)\).

What it does not yet prove:

- that the real corrected cubic/quintic defects used in the two-pair problem are in fact such finite transport-jet functionals;
- any global no-reentry theorem beyond the local quartic–sextic corner.

So the attack has not fully closed the branch, but it has compressed the remaining gap to one very narrow statement.

---

## 6. My honest read of the live next step on Attack B

The best next push is not another abstract parity lemma. It is to identify the actual corrected overlap state on the residual corner and test whether it is built from a finite quotient-visible transport jet.

Concretely, the question is now:

> Is the residual corrected two-pair package on \(\{S=0\}\cap\{K_v=0\}\) determined by finitely many derivatives of the regularized quotient scalar \(Q=J_{u_5}/J_\lambda\)?

If yes, the quartic–sextic local corner is basically done.

If you want, I’ll next turn this into draft-ready theorem/proposition/corollary insertions keyed to the current quotient-transport section, including one proposition for “finite transport-jet quotient descent” and one corollary for “no finite-order hidden reset on the quartic–sextic rung.”

## Assistant (2026-04-21 16:41:11)

I’m drilling into the actual defect formulas and the \(K_v=0\) quotient section in the draft now. The key question is whether the corrected two-pair defects really depend only on a finite quotient-visible transport jet; that is the bridge from the structural theorem to an actual closure step.

_Thought for 4m 3s_

I pushed the attack in the most useful remaining direction, and the main new point is this:

the residual exact fixed-shear corner is even more rigid than “quotient-visible up to \(O(t^2)\).” In fact, if the actual corrected two-pair package is built only from the two individual quotient-visible transport states, then on the involutive branch the interaction part cannot merely be small — it collapses outright.

That gives a sharp new theorem and a sharp negative finding.

---

Let
\[
(h_1,h_2)=(h(t),h(-t)),
\qquad h(0)=a,
\qquad h'(0)\neq 0,
\]
be the residual exact fixed-shear involutive branch near
\[
a\in \{S=0\}\cap\{K_v=0\}.
\]

From the existing quotient-transport package, for each finite \(N\) define the parity-normalized transport state
\[
\mathcal T_N(t):=
\bigl(\Theta_0(t),\Theta_1(t),\dots,\Theta_N(t)\bigr),
\]
with
\[
\Theta_k(t):=t^{-(k\bmod 2)}Q^{(k)}(t),
\qquad
Q(t)=\frac{J_{u_5}(t)}{J_\lambda(t)}=\widehat Q(t^2).
\]
Then each \(\Theta_k\) is even, so
\[
\mathcal T_N(-t)=\mathcal T_N(t)=\widetilde{\mathcal T}_N(t^2).
\]

So the two atoms on the involutive branch carry exactly the same finite quotient-visible transport state.

That lets us attack the actual corrected package directly.

## 1. State-local realization would force exact collapse

Assume there is some finite \(N\) and an analytic map
\[
\mathfrak P_2
=
\mathfrak P_2(a_1,a_2;Y_1,Y_2)
\]
such that the actual corrected two-pair package on the residual corner is given by
\[
\mathcal P_2(t)
=
\mathfrak P_2\!\bigl(a_1(t),a_2(t);\mathcal T_N(h_1(t)),\mathcal T_N(h_2(t))\bigr),
\]
and assume the one-atom package is similarly
\[
F_h=\mathfrak F(\mathcal T_N(h)).
\]

Suppose moreover that this realization satisfies the natural diagonal merger law
\[
\mathfrak P_2(a_1,a_2;Y,Y)=(a_1+a_2)\,\mathfrak F(Y).
\]

Then on the involutive branch,
\[
\mathcal T_N(h_1(t))=\mathcal T_N(h_2(t)),
\]
so
\[
\mathcal P_2(t)
=
\mathfrak P_2\!\bigl(a_1(t),a_2(t);\mathcal T_N(t),\mathcal T_N(t)\bigr)
=
(a_1(t)+a_2(t))\,\mathfrak F(\mathcal T_N(t)).
\]

Therefore the interaction remainder
\[
\mathcal I_2(t):=\mathcal P_2(t)-a_1(t)F_{h_1(t)}-a_2(t)F_{h_2(t)}
\]
is identically zero:
\[
\mathcal I_2(t)\equiv 0.
\]

So in that situation the cubic/quintic/septic defects do not merely satisfy
\[
O((h_1-h_2)^2);
\]
they vanish identically along the residual involutive branch.

That is the strongest local closure statement I can justify.

---

## 2. Meaning for the actual attack

This gives a very sharp criterion:

\[
\boxed{
\text{If the actual corrected two-pair package is state-local in finitely many quotient-visible transport coordinates, the residual }K_v=0\text{ corner is closed.}
}
\]

In particular, the quartic–sextic rung would be dead immediately.

Why? Because on that rung the finite quotient-visible transport state is already determined by \(Q\) alone:
\[
\mathcal T_N(t)=\mathbf F_N(Q(t)),
\]
and the involution gives equal state on both atoms. A state-local two-atom package cannot distinguish the two sides of the involution.

So any surviving residual exact fixed-shear obstruction must use something more than the two separate one-atom quotient-visible transport states.

That is the key negative finding.

---

## 3. The real remaining obstruction is now very specific

The attack now shows that any still-live obstruction on
\[
\{S=0\}\cap\{K_v=0\}
\]
must be one of the following.

First, the actual corrected two-pair package may depend on genuinely relational two-atom data, not recoverable from the two separate quotient-visible transport states.

Second, it may depend on infinitely deep transport information rather than any finite transport jet.

Third, it may fail to satisfy the exact diagonal merger law when expressed only through those transported states.

So the exact remaining mixed-corner burden is no longer vague. It is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Find the first genuinely relational or provenance-sensitive two-atom input that survives after quotient-visible transport descent.}
}
\]

That is the mixed-corner analogue of the nonmixed “first non-universal source-coupled invariant” problem.

---

## 4. A weaker but still useful variant

Even without full package realization, you still get a strong conditional theorem.

Suppose the actual cubic/quintic defects satisfy
\[
E_{12}^{(3)}(t)=\mathfrak e_3\!\bigl(a_1(t),a_2(t),\mathcal T_N(t)\bigr),
\qquad
E_{12}^{(5)}(t)=\mathfrak e_5\!\bigl(a_1(t),a_2(t),\mathcal T_N(t)\bigr),
\]
for analytic \(\mathfrak e_3,\mathfrak e_5\), and suppose they vanish at the diagonal state:
\[
\mathfrak e_3(a_1(0),a_2(0),\mathcal T_N(0))=0,
\qquad
\mathfrak e_5(a_1(0),a_2(0),\mathcal T_N(0))=0.
\]
Since
\[
\mathcal T_N(t)=\mathcal T_N(0)+O(t^2),
\]
it follows immediately that
\[
E_{12}^{(3)}(t)=O(t^2),
\qquad
E_{12}^{(5)}(t)=O(t^2),
\]
hence
\[
E_{12}^{(3)}=O((h_1-h_2)^2),
\qquad
E_{12}^{(5)}=O((h_1-h_2)^2).
\]
So the present defect-scale closeness theorem closes the branch.

Thus there are really two closure levels:

- state-local package realization \(\Rightarrow\) defects vanish identically on the involutive branch;
- state-local defect realization \(\Rightarrow\) defects are quadratic in the separation and the branch is excluded.

---

## 5. What I think is the strongest handback from this attack

The strongest honest handback is:

The exact fixed-shear \(K_v=0\) involutive corner is now rigid enough that any finite-order two-pair model built only from the two separate quotient-visible transport states would already collapse. So any genuinely remaining obstruction there cannot be a hidden finite-order reset inside the descended transport jet itself. It must come from additional relational two-atom structure, or from non-finite-order dependence, not from the quotient-visible transport state alone.

That is a real structural advance. It narrows the remaining mixed-corner problem substantially.

The next best push is to inspect the actual corrected cubic/quintic defect formulas and ask a very sharp question:

do they use only the two individual transported states, or is there a first genuinely relational two-atom quantity that survives on the residual fixed-shear corner?

Here is the full handback on **Attack B** — what I attacked, what I think is now genuinely established, what is only conditional, and what the remaining gap really is.

The target was the mixed residual corner, specifically the **exact fixed-shear slice**
\[
\{S=0\}\cap\{K_v=0\},
\]
where the two-point work suggests an involutive parametrization
\[
(h_1,h_2)=(h(t),h(-t)),
\qquad h(0)=a,\quad h'(0)\neq 0.

The goal was to prove an **involution descent / quotient-visible transport theorem**: namely, that the controlling residual transport data is even under \(t\mapsto -t\), hence descends to the quotient variable
\[
u=t^2,
\]
so the remaining overlap problem is no longer a free two-sided \(t\)-germ.

What I found is that this attack works, and in a stronger form than the minimal target.

## 1. The basic quotient descent does go through

The current draft already has the regularized quotient transport scalar
\[
Q(t):=\frac{J_{u_5}(t)}{J_\lambda(t)},
\]
and on the involutive branch one has
\[
Q(t)=\widehat Q(t^2).
\]
So \(Q\) is even.

I pushed that further by introducing the parity-normalized transport jets
\[
\Theta_k(t):=t^{-(k\bmod 2)}Q^{(k)}(t),\qquad k\ge 0.
\]
Thus
\[
\Theta_0=Q,\qquad
\Theta_1=t^{-1}Q',\qquad
\Theta_2=Q'',\qquad
\Theta_3=t^{-1}Q''',\dots
\]

Because \(Q\) is even, each \(Q^{(k)}\) has the usual parity, and every odd analytic germ is divisible by \(t\). Therefore each \(\Theta_k\) is again even analytic, so
\[
\Theta_k(t)=\widetilde\Theta_k(t^2)
\]
for a unique analytic quotient germ \(\widetilde\Theta_k(u)\).

That gives the first real theorem-level gain:

> **Finite transport-jet quotient descent:** every parity-normalized finite transport jet on the exact fixed-shear involutive branch descends analytically to the quotient variable \(u=t^2\).

So the local transport state is not a two-sided \(t\)-state anymore. It is a one-parameter quotient state.

A particularly canonical descended scalar is
\[
X(t):=\frac{Q'(t)}{t}.
\]
This is automatically even, and in fact
\[
X(t)=2\,\widehat Q'(t^2)=2\,\widehat{\mathcal D}(t^2).
\]
So the specific “controlling residual scalar” envisioned in Attack B is indeed quotient-visible.

## 2. On the first surviving rung, the whole finite transport state is controlled by \(Q\) alone

I then specialized to the quartic–sextic rung
\[
(m,n)=(4,6),
\qquad (r,e)=(2,0),
\]
which is the first genuinely live residual rung in the present package.

The draft’s current setup already implies
\[
\widehat Q'(0)=\widehat{\mathcal D}(0)\neq 0.
\]
So \(\widehat Q\) is a local analytic coordinate in the quotient variable \(u\). Once that is true, every descended jet coordinate \(\widetilde\Theta_k(u)\) can be re-expressed as an analytic function of \(\widehat Q(u)\), hence of \(Q(t)\) itself:
\[
\Theta_k(t)=F_k(Q(t)).
\]

This gives a much stronger local compression:

> **Rank-one transport-state theorem on the quartic–sextic rung:** every finite parity-normalized transport-jet scalar is an analytic function of the single scalar \(Q\) alone.

So on that first surviving residual rung, there is no hidden second local transport parameter. The entire finite transport state has local rank \(1\).

That is stronger than “some scalar descends.” It says the whole finite-order transport package is locally controlled by one quotient coordinate.

## 3. No finite-order hidden reset

From that, I extracted a clean structural consequence.

Let
\[
\mathcal T_N(t):=(\Theta_0(t),\dots,\Theta_N(t))
\]
be the finite quotient-visible transport state up to order \(N\). On the quartic–sextic rung, since
\[
\mathcal T_N(t)=\mathbf F_N(Q(t))
\]
for some analytic map \(\mathbf F_N\), equality of finite transport state implies equality of \(Q\). But \(Q(t)=\widehat Q(t^2)\), and \(\widehat Q\) is locally injective in \(u=t^2\). Therefore
\[
\mathcal T_N(t_1)=\mathcal T_N(t_2)
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
t_2=\pm t_1.
\]

So the only local duplication in the finite transport state is the known involution pair \(t\leftrightarrow -t\). There is no additional local reset point.

This gives:

> **No finite-order hidden reset theorem:** on the quartic–sextic residual corner, no finite quotient-visible transport state can produce a third local reset beyond the involution symmetry itself.

That is a real sharpening of the current picture. It rules out a whole class of local hidden-state mechanisms.

## 4. Strong conditional closure: if the actual defects are finite transport-state functionals, the corner is closed

The next step was to connect this structural theorem to the actual overlap defects.

There are two versions of the conditional closure.

### 4a. Weaker version: state-local defect realization

Suppose the actual corrected cubic/quintic residual defects satisfy
\[
E_{12}^{(3)}(t)=\mathfrak e_3(\mathcal T_N(t),a_1(t),a_2(t)),
\qquad
E_{12}^{(5)}(t)=\mathfrak e_5(\mathcal T_N(t),a_1(t),a_2(t)),
\]
for analytic functionals \(\mathfrak e_3,\mathfrak e_5\), and vanish on the diagonal state.

Since
\[
\mathcal T_N(t)=\mathcal T_N(0)+O(t^2),
\]
it follows that
\[
E_{12}^{(3)}(t)=O(t^2),
\qquad
E_{12}^{(5)}(t)=O(t^2).
\]
And because
\[
h(t)-h(-t)=2h'(0)t+O(t^3),
\]
this becomes
\[
E_{12}^{(3)}=O((h_1-h_2)^2),
\qquad
E_{12}^{(5)}=O((h_1-h_2)^2).
\]

That is exactly the scale needed for the existing defect-closeness exclusion mechanism. So under this hypothesis, the residual branch is excluded.

### 4b. Stronger version: full two-pair package state-locality

I then pushed a stronger conditional statement.

Suppose the actual corrected two-pair package is built from the two individual finite transport states,
\[
\mathcal P_2(t)=
\mathfrak P_2\!\bigl(a_1(t),a_2(t);\mathcal T_N(h_1(t)),\mathcal T_N(h_2(t))\bigr),
\]
and suppose the package satisfies the natural diagonal merger law
\[
\mathfrak P_2(a_1,a_2;Y,Y)=(a_1+a_2)\mathfrak F(Y),
\]
where \(\mathfrak F(Y)\) is the corresponding one-atom package.

But on the involutive branch we have
\[
\mathcal T_N(h_1(t))=\mathcal T_N(h_2(t)),
\]
because each \(\Theta_k\) is even. Therefore the two-pair package collapses exactly to the merged one-atom package. The interaction remainder
\[
\mathcal I_2(t):=
\mathcal P_2(t)-a_1(t)F_{h_1(t)}-a_2(t)F_{h_2(t)}
\]
must vanish identically:
\[
\mathcal I_2(t)\equiv 0.
\]

So under this stronger hypothesis the residual corner does not merely satisfy a quadratic smallness estimate. The interaction part dies identically along the involutive branch.

That is the strongest closure statement I got out of the attack.

## 5. The main negative finding

This attack also produced a sharp negative result, and I think it is important.

If the exact fixed-shear residual corner is still genuinely live, then the obstruction cannot come from any hidden finite-order behavior inside the quotient-visible transport jet itself.

More concretely:

- it cannot come from a second local transport variable on the quartic–sextic rung;
- it cannot come from a “third reset” inside any finite parity-normalized transport state;
- it cannot come from a two-pair model built only from the two separate quotient-visible one-atom states, assuming the natural merger law.

So any still-live obstruction on
\[
\{S=0\}\cap\{K_v=0\}
\]
must use something beyond that descended transport package.

That narrows the remaining possibilities a lot.

## 6. What the real remaining gap now is

The remaining gap is now very precise.

To actually close the corner from Attack B, one still needs to show one of the following.

First possibility: the actual corrected cubic/quintic defects are indeed analytic functionals of a finite quotient-visible transport state. Then the weaker closure above excludes the branch.

Second possibility: the full corrected two-pair package is state-local in the stronger sense above. Then the interaction remainder vanishes identically, which is even better.

If neither is true, then the only way the corner can remain live is that the real two-pair package depends on additional structure not captured by the two separate descended one-atom states. That extra structure would have to be one of the following types:

- genuinely relational two-atom data;
- provenance-sensitive data not seen by the universal quotient-transport state;
- or possibly non-finite-order dependence.

This is the central negative finding of the attack:

> any remaining obstruction on the exact fixed-shear residual corner must come from the first genuinely relational or provenance-sensitive two-atom input that survives after quotient-visible transport descent.

So Attack B did not fully close the corner outright, but it did compress the remaining burden to one narrow and very concrete issue.

## 7. Bottom line

The strongest honest summary is this.

I upgraded the fixed-shear involutive reduction from a single even scalar to a full **finite transport-jet quotient descent theorem**. On the quartic–sextic rung, that sharpens further to a **rank-one transport-state theorem**: every finite parity-normalized transport scalar is locally a function of \(Q\) alone. From that I got a **no finite-order hidden reset theorem**. Then I showed that if the actual corrected defect package is finite-state-local in the descended transport variables, the branch is excluded; and if the full two-pair package is state-local with the natural merger law, the interaction remainder actually vanishes identically on the involutive branch.

So the real mathematical gain is:

- the exact fixed-shear \(K_v=0\) corner is now much more rigid than before;
- the whole finite transport package is quotient-visible;
- on the first live rung it has local rank \(1\);
- no hidden finite-order local reset survives there;
- any remaining obstruction must come from genuinely relational or provenance-sensitive two-atom structure, not from the descended transport state alone.

That is the current handback.

\[

That is a useful sharpening for nonmixed 4-point, because it tells us exactly where order-7 can still bite and where it cannot.

The two-point chat has not produced an unconditional closure, but it has done something nearly as useful strategically. It has shown that the geometry itself is no longer the main obstacle. The residual mixed corner is now a quotient-diagonal, rank-one, no-finite-hidden-reset problem. Therefore the remaining burden is on the actual corrected package: source-level merger, state-locality, collision-functoriality, or the first surviving relational two-atom invariant.  

For our nonmixed 4-point attack, that strongly reinforces the agenda you already wrote down as Attack A. The thing to hunt is the first non-universal source-coupled invariant — something that fails in the universal normalized model. The two-point handback is basically evidence that the universal finite-order transport geometry has been squeezed dry. What remains, in both lanes, is the first genuinely relational / provenance-sensitive obstruction.

My practical recommendation is: import this as a strategic lemma, not as closure. Treat the following as established working facts unless contradicted by the draft:

1. universal finite-order transport geometry on the mixed residual corner is exhausted;
2. local hidden-reset mechanisms in that descended package are gone;
3. any surviving obstruction must be relational, provenance-sensitive, or beyond finite transport order;
4. the cancellation chart, not the naive diagonal chart, is the right local model for close bad two-point cores.

Here’s a draft note to hand to Attack A.

The main handback from two-point is that the mixed residual geometry has now been compressed much further than the draft currently reflects, and that changes what kind of theorem is worth chasing on nonmixed 4-point. On the residual exact fixed-shear corner \(\{S=0\}\cap\{K_v=0\}\), the branch is no longer a free two-sided local branch: after parity reduction it is involutive / quotient-diagonal, \(Q(t)=\widehat Q(t^2)\), every parity-normalized finite transport jet descends to the quotient variable \(u=t^2\), and on the first surviving quartic–sextic rung the entire finite transport state has local rank \(1\). In particular there is no “third local reset” hiding inside any finite descended transport state. So that whole universal finite-order transport geometry now looks squeezed dry.  

The most important consequence for your lane is negative but very useful: if anything is still live after this compression, it cannot be coming from another universal scalar/discriminant/sign argument inside the already-descended package. The two-point attack now strongly suggests that any surviving obstruction must come from the **first genuinely relational or provenance-sensitive two-atom datum** that survives quotient-visible transport descent, or else from some non-finite-order dependence. That is exactly the kind of object Attack A should now be trying to isolate on the nonmixed 4-point side as the first **non-universal source-coupled invariant**.  

A second correction that matters strategically: near a genuine close bad two-point branch on a good patch \(J\Subset\{c\neq 0\}\), the right base locus is not the ordinary diagonal \((h_1,h_2)=(h,h)\) with arbitrary total amplitude. It is the **collision-cancellation locus**
\[
\delta:=h_2-h_1=0,\qquad \lambda:=-\frac{a_2}{a_1}=1,
\]
because the cubic identity forces \(a_1c(h_1)+a_2c(h_2)\approx 0\), hence \(a_1+a_2\approx 0\) when \(h_1\approx h_2\) and \(c\neq 0\). In the blow-up chart
\[
m=\frac{h_1+h_2}{2},\qquad \delta=h_2-h_1,\qquad \mu=\lambda-1,
\]
the first-order source direction is the projective tangent datum
\[
\Theta_{m,\theta}=\cos\theta\,D_m+\sin\theta\,D_m'.
\]
So if Attack A ends up formulating a source-coupled invariant near coincidence, it should be phrased against this cancellation/blow-up chart, not against the naive merged-source diagonal. 

This also sharpens what order-7 should mean in your lane. The honest septic datum is not full order-7 equality of representatives, but the quotient class
\[
[A_7^{\mathfrak f}]\in \mathfrak f/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]
Once two corrected germs agree through cubic and quintic order and differ only by an odd reparametrization plus the already-quotiented lower gauge, the septic quotient defect vanishes formally. But cubic/quintic merger alone does **not** force that odd-reparametrization comparability; the transverse quotient-septic class is exactly the obstruction. So the right theorem target is not “prove septic equality,” but rather “prove same reduced image germ at coincidence,” or more concretely, prove a collision-functoriality statement at the corrected-block level that makes the same-image-germ conclusion formal. This is one place where a genuinely non-universal invariant could first appear.  

My recommendation for Attack A is therefore:

1. Treat the present universal source package as exhausted. Do not spend cycles trying to squeeze one more contradiction out of the same normalized scalar/discriminant data; two-point now gives strong evidence that those mechanisms are already universalized away. 

2. Test candidate invariants by the brutal question: can this still be realized in the universal normalized lift? If yes, it is probably not your closure theorem. If no, you may have found the first truly RH-specific source-coupled datum. The natural places to look remain quotient-septic / mixed-level objects, but only in a provenance-sensitive form, not as arbitrary quotient-septic geometry. This recommendation is exactly aligned with the two-point conclusion that what remains must be relational or provenance-sensitive. 

3. Aim for one of these theorem shapes:
   - a **same reduced image germ at coincidence** theorem;
   - a **collision-functoriality** theorem for the corrected block triple on the collision/cancellation locus;
   - or an **exclusion theorem for the first relational two-atom invariant** surviving after descent.
   Any of those would interact correctly with the order-7 quotient class and with the corrected two-point picture.  

4. Keep the labor split clean: on the residual mixed corner, cubic and quintic are already the decisive local orders for exclusion if state-locality holds; septic is not central there. By contrast, for the strong finite-order source-level merger route, septic still matters precisely through the quotient class. So if Attack A uses order 7, it should be because it is isolating a genuinely new relational/provenance-sensitive obstruction, not because it is trying to re-run a lower-order universal argument. 

In one sentence: the two-point handback says the geometry is no longer the obstacle; the remaining burden is to identify the first **non-universal, relational, provenance-sensitive source-coupled invariant** that survives after all the quotient-visible transport descent and cancellation-chart compression. That is the exact kind of object Attack A should now hunt.

_Thought for 4m 27s_

Yes. I think there is one more real push, and it sharpens the residual-corner picture in a useful way.

The new point is this:

the first blown-up **relational** datum from the two-point cancellation chart also descends through the involution. So even the projective tangent-direction family from the cancellation blow-up is **not** a new two-sided local degree of freedom on the residual exact fixed-shear corner. The genuinely remaining obstruction has to sit even further out. That fits the two-point handback very closely.  

Here is the argument.

On the close bad-core cancellation chart identified by the two-point work, the right local variables are
\[
m:=\frac{h_1+h_2}{2},\qquad
\delta:=h_2-h_1,\qquad
\mu:=\lambda-1,
\qquad
\lambda:=-\frac{a_2}{a_1},
\]
and the first-order source datum is the blow-up direction of
\[
D_{h_1}-\lambda D_{h_2}.
\]
The handback already says this is the correct chart, and that the first-order projective source direction is the real local datum near cancellation, not the naive ordinary diagonal. 

Now combine that with the residual exact fixed-shear involution picture:
\[
(h_1,h_2)=(h(t),h(-t)),
\qquad h(0)=a,\quad h'(0)\neq 0.
\]
Then automatically
\[
\delta(t)=h(-t)-h(t)
\]
is odd, with
\[
\delta(t)=-2h'(0)t+O(t^3),
\]
so in particular
\[
\delta(t)=t\,\widehat\delta(t^2),
\qquad \widehat\delta(0)\neq 0.
\]

The amplitude variable needs a better coordinate than \(\mu=\lambda-1\), because under label-swap one has
\[
\lambda\longmapsto \frac1\lambda,
\]
not \(\lambda\mapsto -\lambda\). So the right normalized cancellation coordinate is
\[
\omega:=\frac{\lambda-1}{\lambda+1}.
\]
This is exactly the Möbius oddification of the cancellation locus \(\lambda=1\). Under swap,
\[
\omega\longmapsto -\omega.
\]
So after choosing a swap-compatible normalization of the branch,
\[
\omega(-t)=-\omega(t).
\]
Hence
\[
\omega(t)=t\,\widehat\omega(t^2)
\]
for an analytic quotient germ \(\widehat\omega\).

So both first-order cancellation variables are odd:
\[
\omega(t)=t\,\widehat\omega(u),\qquad
\delta(t)=t\,\widehat\delta(u),\qquad u=t^2.
\]

That already gives a new theorem-level compression:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The blown-up cancellation projective direction }[\omega:\delta]
\text{ is quotient-visible.}
}
\]

Indeed,
\[
[\omega(t):\delta(t)]
=
[\widehat\omega(t^2):\widehat\delta(t^2)].
\]

Because \(\widehat\delta(0)\neq 0\), we can pass to an affine slope:
\[
\kappa(t):=\frac{2\omega(t)}{\delta(t)}.
\]
Then \(\kappa\) is even analytic:
\[
\kappa(t)=\widehat\kappa(t^2).
\]

Now expand the first-order source difference in this chart. Using
\[
h_1=m-\frac{\delta}{2},\qquad h_2=m+\frac{\delta}{2},
\]
we have
\[
D_{h_1}=D_m-\frac{\delta}{2}D_m'+O(\delta^2),
\qquad
D_{h_2}=D_m+\frac{\delta}{2}D_m'+O(\delta^2).
\]
Therefore
\[
D_{h_1}-\lambda D_{h_2}
=
(1-\lambda)D_m-\frac{1+\lambda}{2}\delta\,D_m'
+O\!\big((|\lambda-1|+|\delta|)^2\big).
\]
Since
\[
1-\lambda=-(1+\lambda)\omega,
\]
this becomes
\[
\frac{D_{h_1}-\lambda D_{h_2}}{1+\lambda}
=
-\omega D_m-\frac{\delta}{2}D_m'
+O\!\big((|\omega|+|\delta|)^2\big).
\]
Dividing by \(\delta/2\) gives
\[
\frac{D_{h_1}-\lambda D_{h_2}}{(1+\lambda)\delta/2}
=
-\kappa(t)\,D_m-D_m'
+O(|\delta|+|\omega|).
\]

So the first blown-up source direction is governed by the single even scalar
\[
\kappa(t)=\frac{2\omega(t)}{\delta(t)}.
\]

This is the new structural gain:

the first-order cancellation direction from the two-point blow-up is not an extra local odd datum. It also descends to the quotient.

Now combine that with the quartic–sextic rung. On that rung we already had
\[
Q(t)=\widehat Q(t^2),
\qquad
\widehat Q'(0)\neq 0,
\]
so \(\widehat Q\) is a local analytic coordinate in \(u=t^2\). The two-point handback also already established that the residual transport state has local rank \(1\) there.  

Therefore
\[
\widehat\kappa(u)=K(\widehat Q(u))
\]
for some analytic germ \(K\). Equivalently,
\[
\kappa(t)=K(Q(t)).
\]

So on the quartic–sextic residual corner, even the **first blown-up relational source angle** is locally controlled by the same single quotient scalar \(Q\).

That is stronger than what I had before.

Before, the conclusion was:

- no hidden finite-order reset inside the descended one-atom transport state.

Now the stronger conclusion is:

- not even the first-order cancellation/blow-up direction furnishes a second local degree of freedom.

So the first genuinely surviving obstruction cannot be:

1. a second local transport scalar;
2. a hidden finite-order reset inside the transport jet;
3. the first blown-up cancellation angle \([\omega:\delta]\) or its affine slope \(\kappa\).

Those are all already quotient-visible and, on the quartic–sextic rung, locally rank-one functions of \(Q\).

That leaves a much narrower target.

The remaining obstruction, if any, must live in one of these places:

- higher-order **transverse relational** data beyond the first blow-up direction;
- a provenance-sensitive package-level input not recoverable from \((Q,\kappa)\);
- or a same-image-germ / quotient-septic obstruction of the kind the two-point handback points to.  

So my honest updated handback is:

the residual exact fixed-shear corner is even more rigid than we thought. Not only the one-atom transport state, but also the first cancellation-chart relational direction, descends through the involution. On the quartic–sextic rung both are locally controlled by the same quotient coordinate \(Q\). Therefore any still-live obstruction must begin strictly beyond first-order blown-up cancellation geometry.

That gives a very sharp next attack:

hunt the **first higher-order relational datum not determined by \((Q,\kappa)\)**. In draft language, that means either a same reduced image germ theorem, or the first quotient-septic / collision-functoriality obstruction that survives after both transport descent and cancellation-angle descent.

Yes. I think there is a genuinely sharper push now, and it uses the cancellation-chart correction from two-point in exactly the right way.

The new point is this:

on the residual exact fixed-shear corner, the **entire first blown-up interaction layer is parity-forbidden**. So the first surviving relational obstruction, if any, cannot live in the tangent-direction family at all. It has to begin at **second transverse order or higher**.

That is stronger than what I had before.

The reason starts from the corrected local chart that the two-point handback identified as the right one near a close cancelling branch:
\[
m:=\frac{h_1+h_2}{2},\qquad
\delta:=h_2-h_1,\qquad
\lambda:=-\frac{a_2}{a_1},
\]
with collision-cancellation locus
\[
\delta=0,\qquad \lambda=1.
\]
And, as I noted last turn, the right swap-linearized amplitude coordinate is not \(\mu=\lambda-1\), but
\[
\omega:=\frac{\lambda-1}{\lambda+1},
\]
because under atom-swap one has
\[
(h_1,h_2,\lambda)\longmapsto (h_2,h_1,\lambda^{-1}),
\]
hence
\[
m\longmapsto m,\qquad
\delta\longmapsto -\delta,\qquad
\omega\longmapsto -\omega.
\]

So \((m,\omega,\delta)\) is the correct local analytic chart for the cancellation regime, with swap acting by simultaneous sign-flip on the two transverse coordinates. This is exactly the geometric correction the two-point handback emphasized. 

Now here is the theorem-shaped attack.

Assume the actual corrected cubic/quintic defects admit local analytic representatives
\[
E_{12}^{(3)}=\mathcal E_3(m,\omega,\delta),
\qquad
E_{12}^{(5)}=\mathcal E_5(m,\omega,\delta)
\]
near the collision-cancellation locus, and assume the natural package symmetry
\[
\mathcal E_j(m,-\omega,-\delta)=\mathcal E_j(m,\omega,\delta)
\qquad (j=3,5),
\]
together with exact vanishing on the collision locus
\[
\mathcal E_j(m,0,0)=0.
\]

Then every monomial in the Taylor series of \(\mathcal E_j\) must have **even total degree** in \((\omega,\delta)\), because simultaneous sign-flip kills all odd total degrees. Since the constant term also vanishes, the linear part vanishes automatically. Therefore
\[
\mathcal E_j(m,\omega,\delta)=O(\omega^2+\delta^2).
\]

That is the key gain.

It says the first blown-up interaction layer — the linear tangent-direction layer — cannot appear at all under the natural symmetry. So the naive first-order family
\[
\Theta_{m,\theta}\sim \cos\theta\,D_m+\sin\theta\,D_m'
\]
cannot be the surviving obstruction. The tangent-direction family is parity-sterile.

Now restrict to the residual exact fixed-shear involutive branch
\[
(h_1,h_2)=(h(t),h(-t)).
\]
Then, as before,
\[
\delta(t)=h(-t)-h(t)=t\,\widehat\delta(t^2),
\qquad
\omega(t)=t\,\widehat\omega(t^2),
\]
so both transverse chart coordinates are odd and hence
\[
\omega(t)^2+\delta(t)^2=O(t^2).
\]
Therefore
\[
E_{12}^{(3)}(t)=O(t^2),
\qquad
E_{12}^{(5)}(t)=O(t^2).
\]
Since \(\delta=h_2-h_1\sim -2h'(0)t\), this becomes
\[
E_{12}^{(3)}=O((h_1-h_2)^2),
\qquad
E_{12}^{(5)}=O((h_1-h_2)^2).
\]
So the existing good-patch defect-closeness mechanism excludes the branch.

In other words:

if the actual corrected defects are analytic in the **correct** collision chart \((m,\omega,\delta)\), swap-invariant, and vanish on the collision-cancellation locus, then the residual exact fixed-shear corner is already closed.

This is better than the earlier “evenness in \(t\)” criterion, because it explains where that evenness really comes from. It is not just involution in the source parameter. It is the intrinsic swap parity of the cancellation chart.

And it gives a stronger negative finding.

Before, the conclusion was that no hidden finite-order reset survives inside the quotient-visible transport state, and that even the first blown-up source angle \(\kappa=2\omega/\delta\) is quotient-visible and locally controlled by \(Q\). turn8file4

Now we can say more:

the **entire first transverse blow-up order** is unavailable. So any still-live obstruction on
\[
\{S=0\}\cap\{K_v=0\}
\]
must begin at second order in the cancellation variables. It cannot be:

- a second hidden transport scalar;
- a third reset inside the finite transport jet;
- the first cancellation angle \([\omega:\delta]\);
- or any linear blown-up interaction law depending on \((m,\kappa)\).

All of those are dead.

So the first genuinely surviving relational datum, if it exists, must be a **quadratic-or-higher transverse invariant**. That matches the two-point handback’s broader conclusion that what remains is package-level and relational, not geometric. turn8file6

This also interacts nicely with the septic story.

The two-point handback already sharpened the order-7 target to the quotient class
\[
[A_7^{\mathfrak f}]\in \mathfrak f/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f},
\]
and said the honest remaining theorem is same reduced image germ at coincidence, or collision-functoriality on the cancellation locus. turn8file6

What the new parity argument adds is:

if such a quotient-septic obstruction survives, it cannot appear as a first-order blown-up defect in the cancellation direction. It must enter only at second transverse order or higher.

That narrows the real target a lot.

So my updated attack summary is:

the residual exact fixed-shear corner is now even more rigid than before. Not only is the one-atom transport package quotient-visible and rank-one on the quartic-sextic rung, but the correct cancellation-chart parity also kills the entire first blown-up relational layer. Therefore any remaining obstruction must start at **quadratic transverse order**, most plausibly as the first genuinely relational/provenance-sensitive package datum — exactly the sort of same-image-germ / collision-functoriality / quotient-septic obstruction the two-point handback singled out. turn8file6

I think the next clean theorem to try is:

> **Quadratic blow-up obstruction theorem.**  
> Show that the first nontrivial transverse coefficient in the swap-even cancellation-chart expansion is itself quotient-visible or functorial enough to collapse on coincidence.

If that lands, the residual mixed corner is probably done.

_Thought for 1m 27s_

I think there is one more real compression, and it is better than just “the defects are \(O(\delta^2)\).”

The right statement is:

on the residual exact fixed-shear involutive branch, any swap-even analytic defect on the cancellation chart is not only quadratic in the transverse separation — its **entire quadratic coefficient is quotient-visible**, and on the quartic–sextic rung it is locally a function of \(Q\) alone. That pushes the remaining obstruction one rung further out. This is exactly in the spirit of the two-point handback’s correction to the cancellation chart and its quotient-visible transport descent picture.  

Here is the clean formulation.

Take the correct cancellation chart near a close cancelling branch:
\[
m:=\frac{h_1+h_2}{2},\qquad
\delta:=h_2-h_1,\qquad
\lambda:=-\frac{a_2}{a_1},\qquad
\omega:=\frac{\lambda-1}{\lambda+1}.
\]
Under atom-swap,
\[
m\mapsto m,\qquad \delta\mapsto -\delta,\qquad \omega\mapsto -\omega.
\]

Now suppose the actual corrected cubic or quintic defect admits a local analytic representative
\[
E(m,\omega,\delta)
\]
with the natural symmetry
\[
E(m,-\omega,-\delta)=E(m,\omega,\delta),
\]
and vanishes on the collision-cancellation locus:
\[
E(m,0,0)=0.
\]

Then its Taylor expansion has only even total degree in \((\omega,\delta)\), and no constant term. So
\[
E(m,\omega,\delta)
=
\sum_{\substack{a,b\ge 0\\ a+b\ge 2\\ a+b\ \mathrm{even}}}
c_{ab}(m)\,\omega^a\delta^b.
\]
That already kills the entire linear blown-up layer.

\[
(h_1,h_2)=(h(t),h(-t)).
\]
Then
\[
\delta(t)=t\,\widehat\delta(t^2),\qquad \widehat\delta(0)\neq 0,
\]
and, after swap-compatible normalization,
\[
\omega(t)=t\,\widehat\omega(t^2).
\]
So every monomial \(\omega^a\delta^b\) with \(a+b\ge 2\) contributes at least a factor \(t^2\). Hence
\[
E(t)=t^2\,\widehat E(t^2)
\]
for some analytic quotient germ \(\widehat E\).

Because \(\delta(t)=t\,\widehat\delta(t^2)\) with \(\widehat\delta(0)\neq 0\), this can be rewritten more sharply as
\[
\boxed{
E(t)=\delta(t)^2\,H(t^2)
}
\]
for an analytic quotient-visible scalar \(H\).

That is stronger than the earlier \(E=O(\delta^2)\) statement. It says the whole first surviving transverse coefficient already descends to the quotient.

Now specialize to the first live rung
\[
(m,n)=(4,6)\iff (r,e)=(2,0).
\]
There we already know the quotient scalar
\[
Q(t)=\widehat Q(t^2)
\]
has
\[
\widehat Q'(0)\neq 0,
\]
so \(\widehat Q\) is a local analytic coordinate in \(u=t^2\). Therefore
\[
H(t^2)=\mathcal H(Q(t))
\]
for some analytic germ \(\mathcal H\), and thus
\[
\boxed{
E(t)=\delta(t)^2\,\mathcal H(Q(t)).
}
\]

That is the new structural gain.

It means that even if a residual defect survives the swap-parity kill, its first possible term is not an arbitrary quadratic relational datum. On the quartic–sextic rung it is forced into a **single-scalar quadratic law** controlled by \(Q\).

So the following things are now dead on the residual exact fixed-shear corner:

- a linear blown-up interaction law in the cancellation variables;
- a new first-order tangent-direction obstruction;
- a quadratic coefficient carrying an independent local degree of freedom beyond the quotient scalar.

The first surviving obstruction, if any, must therefore begin beyond this scalar-controlled quadratic layer. Concretely, it has to come from one of two places.

Either the actual corrected package fails to admit the required local analytic swap-even realization on the cancellation chart.

Or the genuinely new datum is not the existence of a quadratic term at all, but the package-level meaning of the coefficient \(\mathcal H(Q)\): for example, same-image-germ failure, collision-functoriality failure, or the order-7 quotient obstruction that the two-point handback isolated.  

So the best honest handback from this round is:

> On the residual \(K_v=0\) corner, any swap-even analytic cubic/quintic defect restricts along the involutive branch as
> \[
> E(t)=\delta(t)^2\,H(t^2),
> \]
> and on the quartic–sextic rung as
> \[
> E(t)=\delta(t)^2\,\mathcal H(Q(t)).
> \]
> Thus even the first surviving quadratic transverse layer is quotient-visible and rank-one.

That pushes the live target further out. The next attack should not be “is there a quadratic obstruction?” but rather:

> what is the first package-level theorem that forces \(\mathcal H\equiv 0\), or shows that any nonzero \(\mathcal H\) is incompatible with collision functoriality / same reduced image germ / the quotient-septic law?

That feels like the sharpest remaining formulation.

Start from the correct cancellation chart:

(m,\omega,\delta)\mapsto (m,-\omega,-\delta).

- the midpoint \(m\),
- the blown-up projective slope \(\kappa=2\omega/\delta\),
- and the even transverse radius \(\delta^2\).

So the first surviving transverse layer is not an arbitrary quadratic form in two variables. It is already compressed to a one-parameter projective family.

\[
\mathcal H(m,\kappa,0)
=
C(m)+\frac{B(m)}{2}\kappa+\frac{A(m)}{4}\kappa^2.
\]
So the quadratic layer is literally a quadratic polynomial in the single slope \(\kappa\).

That is the first new gain.

\[
(h_1,h_2)=(h(t),h(-t)).

That is more informative than a bare parity argument.

So even the quadratic blow-up coefficient has no independent local degree of freedom. It is just a scalar function of \(Q\).

That is the second new gain.

## Assistant (2026-04-21 18:40:19)

_Thought for 9s_

Here is the full handback for the attack **since the last update**, organized as a mathematical writeup rather than as draft-edit instructions.

The short version is: I pushed the residual exact fixed-shear corner one rung further. The key gain is that, in the correct collision-cancellation chart, the whole first blown-up interaction layer is forced into a **swap-even quadratic law**, and on the involutive \(K_v=0\) branch that quadratic law is already **quotient-visible**. On the quartic–sextic rung, even its coefficient is locally a function of the single quotient scalar \(Q\). So the remaining obstruction, if any, has been pushed **beyond the entire quadratic blow-up layer**. This fits the two-point handback very closely.  

I will write this in a theorem/proposition style.

---

## 1. Setup

We work on the residual exact fixed-shear corner
\[
\{S=0\}\cap\{K_v=0\},
\]
where the two-point handback identifies the correct local involutive picture:
\[
(h_1,h_2)=(h(t),h(-t)),
\qquad h(0)=a,\quad h'(0)\neq 0.
\]
On this branch, the regularized transport quotient satisfies
\[
Q(t):=\frac{J_{u_5}(t)}{J_\lambda(t)}=\widehat Q(t^2),
\]
so \(Q\) is even. More generally, every parity-normalized finite transport jet descends to the quotient variable
\[
u=t^2.
\]
On the first surviving rung
\[
(m,n)=(4,6)\iff (r,e)=(2,0),
\]
one has
\[
\widehat Q'(0)\neq 0,
\]
so \(\widehat Q\) is a local analytic coordinate in \(u\). Thus the whole finite quotient-visible transport state has local rank \(1\).  

The two-point handback also corrected the local bad-core chart: near a close cancelling branch, the right coordinates are not the naive diagonal, but the **collision-cancellation chart**
\[
m:=\frac{h_1+h_2}{2},\qquad
\delta:=h_2-h_1,\qquad
\lambda:=-\frac{a_2}{a_1}\approx 1.
\]
A swap-compatible transverse amplitude coordinate is
\[
\omega:=\frac{\lambda-1}{\lambda+1}.
\]
Under exchange of the two atoms,
\[
(m,\omega,\delta)\mapsto (m,-\omega,-\delta).
\]
This is the correct local chart for the cancellation regime. 

---

## 2. First structural gain: parity kills the whole linear blow-up layer

Let \(E(m,\omega,\delta)\) denote any local analytic corrected defect, such as the corrected cubic or quintic defect, and assume the natural local package symmetry
\[
E(m,-\omega,-\delta)=E(m,\omega,\delta),
\]
together with collision vanishing
\[
E(m,0,0)=0.
\]

Then the Taylor expansion of \(E\) in \((\omega,\delta)\) contains only even total degree and has no constant term. Therefore
\[
E(m,\omega,\delta)
=
A(m)\omega^2+B(m)\omega\delta+C(m)\delta^2
+O\!\big((|\omega|+|\delta|)^4\big).
\]

### Consequence
There is **no linear blown-up interaction layer**.

So the first tangent-direction family from the cancellation blow-up cannot itself be the surviving obstruction. The entire first transverse order is parity-sterile.

That is the first genuine new compression.

---

## 3. Honest blow-up factorization through the projective slope

Introduce the blown-up slope
\[
\kappa:=\frac{2\omega}{\delta},
\]
so that
\[
\omega=\frac{\kappa\delta}{2}.
\]
Substituting into the Taylor expansion, every even monomial \(\omega^a\delta^b\) with \(a+b=2\ell\) becomes
\[
\omega^a\delta^b
=
\delta^{2\ell}\Bigl(\frac{\kappa}{2}\Bigr)^a.
\]
Hence the whole analytic expansion reorganizes as

\[
\boxed{
E(m,\omega,\delta)=\delta^2\,\mathcal H(m,\kappa,\delta^2)
}
\]
for an analytic germ \(\mathcal H\).

This is stronger than the earlier \(E=O(\delta^2)\). It says:

- the first surviving transverse layer is quadratic;
- it depends only on the midpoint \(m\), the projective blow-up slope \(\kappa\), and the even radius \(\delta^2\);
- and its leading coefficient is
\[
\mathcal H(m,\kappa,0)
=
C(m)+\frac{B(m)}{2}\kappa+\frac{A(m)}{4}\kappa^2,
\]
a quadratic polynomial in the single projective variable \(\kappa\).

### Consequence
The quadratic layer is already a **one-projective-parameter law**. It is not an arbitrary quadratic form with two independent transverse degrees of freedom.

That is the second structural gain.

---

## 4. Restriction to the involutive exact fixed-shear branch

On the residual exact fixed-shear involutive branch
\[
(h_1,h_2)=(h(t),h(-t)),
\]
we have
\[
\delta(t)=h(-t)-h(t)=t\,\widehat\delta(t^2),
\qquad \widehat\delta(0)\neq 0,
\]
and, after swap-compatible normalization,
\[
\omega(t)=t\,\widehat\omega(t^2).
\]
Therefore
\[
\kappa(t)=\frac{2\omega(t)}{\delta(t)}
\]
is even analytic:
\[
\kappa(t)=\widehat\kappa(t^2).
\]
Also
\[
m(t)=\frac{h(t)+h(-t)}2
\]
is even:
\[
m(t)=\widehat m(t^2).
\]

Substituting into the factorization above gives

\[
E(t)=\delta(t)^2\,\mathcal H\!\bigl(\widehat m(t^2),\widehat\kappa(t^2),\delta(t)^2\bigr).
\]

Hence there exists an analytic quotient germ \(\widetilde H\) such that

\[
\boxed{
E(t)=\delta(t)^2\,\widetilde H(t^2).
}
\]

This is the strongest unconditional form I got from the symmetry/blow-up analysis itself.

### Consequence
The entire first surviving quadratic transverse layer is already **quotient-visible**.

So even after the parity kill, there is still no genuinely two-sided local quadratic freedom left on the involutive branch.

---

## 5. Quartic–sextic rung: the quadratic coefficient is rank-one

Now specialize to the first live residual rung
\[
(m,n)=(4,6)\iff (r,e)=(2,0).
\]
Here
\[
Q(t)=\widehat Q(t^2),
\qquad \widehat Q'(0)\neq 0.
\]
So \(\widehat Q\) is a local coordinate in \(u=t^2\).

Because \(m(t)\), \(\kappa(t)\), and \(\delta(t)^2\) are all even analytic functions of \(t\), they are analytic functions of \(u=t^2\), hence locally analytic functions of \(Q(t)\). Thus there exist analytic germs \(M,K,D\) such that
\[
m(t)=M(Q(t)),\qquad
\kappa(t)=K(Q(t)),\qquad
\delta(t)^2=D(Q(t)).
\]

Therefore the defect along the branch has the form

\[
\boxed{
E(t)=\delta(t)^2\,\mathcal G(Q(t))
}
\]
for an analytic germ \(\mathcal G\).

Equivalently, even the leading quadratic blow-up coefficient is a scalar function of the **single** quotient transport coordinate \(Q\).

### Consequence
On the quartic–sextic residual corner, the first surviving transverse defect coefficient has **no independent local degree of freedom** beyond \(Q\).

This is stronger than the earlier statement that the finite transport state has rank \(1\): now even the first quadratic relational layer also has rank \(1\).

---

## 6. Conditional closure theorem

This gives the cleanest closure criterion I reached.

### Conditional theorem
Assume the actual corrected cubic/quintic residual defects \(E_{12}^{(3)},E_{12}^{(5)}\) admit local analytic representatives in the collision-cancellation chart \((m,\omega,\delta)\), satisfy
\[
E_j(m,-\omega,-\delta)=E_j(m,\omega,\delta),
\qquad
E_j(m,0,0)=0,
\qquad j=3,5.
\]
Then along the involutive exact fixed-shear branch,
\[
E_{12}^{(3)}(t)=\delta(t)^2\,\widetilde H_3(t^2),
\qquad
E_{12}^{(5)}(t)=\delta(t)^2\,\widetilde H_5(t^2).
\]
Hence
\[
E_{12}^{(3)},E_{12}^{(5)}=O((h_1-h_2)^2).
\]
Therefore the already-established good-patch defect-closeness mechanism excludes the branch.

### Meaning
To close the residual exact fixed-shear corner, one does **not** need a full package-level state-locality theorem. A weaker theorem is enough:

- analyticity in the correct collision chart,
- swap-evenness,
- and collision-vanishing.

If those are true for the actual corrected cubic/quintic defects, the residual corner is done.

That is a substantial simplification of the closure target.

---

## 7. Structural findings

These are the main structural findings from this round.

### (i) Correct local chart
The cancellation regime is governed by the chart
\[
(m,\omega,\delta),\qquad
\omega=\frac{\lambda-1}{\lambda+1},
\]
not the naive merged-source diagonal chart. This matters because swap acts linearly there:
\[
(m,\omega,\delta)\mapsto (m,-\omega,-\delta).
\]

### (ii) Linear blown-up layer is dead
Any swap-even analytic defect with collision vanishing has no linear term in \((\omega,\delta)\). So the first-order tangent-direction layer is automatically sterile.

### (iii) Quadratic layer is one-projective-parameter
The first surviving transverse layer factors as
\[
E=\delta^2\,\mathcal H(m,\kappa,\delta^2),
\qquad
\kappa=\frac{2\omega}{\delta}.
\]
So it is already compressed to one projective slope variable.

### (iv) On the involutive branch, the quadratic layer is quotient-visible
Restricting to \(h_1=h(t)\), \(h_2=h(-t)\) gives
\[
E(t)=\delta(t)^2\,\widetilde H(t^2).
\]

### (v) On the quartic–sextic rung, even that coefficient is rank-one
There,
\[
E(t)=\delta(t)^2\,\mathcal G(Q(t)).
\]
So even the quadratic relational coefficient is locally controlled by the same scalar \(Q\).

---

## 8. Negative findings

These are the strongest negative findings from this round.

### (i) No first-order blown-up obstruction
Any surviving obstruction cannot be a linear tangent-direction law in the cancellation variables.

### (ii) No new projective degree of freedom at quadratic order
Any surviving obstruction cannot be “just” an arbitrary quadratic form in \((\omega,\delta)\), because that whole layer collapses to a one-projective-parameter law, and on the quartic–sextic rung even that parameter is locally a function of \(Q\).

### (iii) The remaining obstruction cannot be generic local geometry
What remains, if anything, is not more local geometric freedom. It has to be something package-level and relational/provenance-sensitive.

This matches the two-point handback’s broader conclusion that the geometry is no longer the obstacle.  

---

## 9. Goodies

These are the mathematically useful “goodies” that came out of the attack.

### (i) A more natural closure target
Instead of proving a strong source-level merger theorem, one could try to prove the weaker but more natural statement:

- the actual corrected cubic/quintic defects are analytic swap-even functions in the collision chart,
- and vanish on the collision locus.

That alone would already close the residual exact fixed-shear corner.

### (ii) Exact factorization shape
The canonical factorization
\[
E=\delta^2\,\mathcal H(m,\kappa,\delta^2)
\]
is much cleaner than a mere \(O(\delta^2)\) estimate. It identifies the precise shape of the first possible surviving term.

### (iii) Rank-one control persists one rung further
Previously the rank-one picture applied to the descended transport state. Now it also applies to the first quadratic relational layer:
\[
E=\delta^2\,\mathcal G(Q).
\]

That pushes the live obstruction one rung further out.

---

## 10. Honest remaining gap

This attack did **not** prove unconditional closure.

The remaining gap is now very precise. To finish the residual exact fixed-shear corner, one still needs to show that the **actual corrected defects** really satisfy the hypotheses used above:

1. local analyticity in the collision-cancellation chart;
2. swap-evenness under \((\omega,\delta)\mapsto(-\omega,-\delta)\);
3. vanishing on the collision-cancellation locus.

If those fail, then the residual obstruction must come from a genuinely more package-level datum, which is exactly what the two-point handback points to:

- same reduced image germ,
- collision functoriality,
- or the transverse quotient-septic obstruction
\[
[A_7^{\mathfrak f}]\in \mathfrak f/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]
 

So the sharpest honest summary is:

> The residual exact fixed-shear corner has now been reduced to a **quadratic, swap-even, quotient-visible collision law**, and on the quartic–sextic rung even that quadratic coefficient is a function of the single quotient scalar \(Q\). Therefore any still-live obstruction must begin **beyond the entire quadratic blow-up layer** and must be genuinely package-level, relational, or provenance-sensitive.

That is the full state of the attack since the last update.

_Thought for 9s_

I’ve read both updates, and they fit the direction of the attack very well. My read is that they sharpen the picture in three important ways and also suggest one place where we should be careful not to overclaim.  

The main convergence is this: all three chats are now saying the same strategic thing from slightly different angles. The residual mixed \(2\)-point corner
\[
\{S=0\}\cap\{K_v=0\}
\]
has been compressed so far that the remaining burden is no longer ordinary local geometry. The quotient-diagonal / involutive reduction, the even quotient transport scalar
\[
Q(t)=\widehat Q(t^2),
\]
the finite transport-jet quotient descent, and the quartic–sextic rank-one theorem together mean that the universal finite-order local state is basically exhausted there. Any still-live obstruction has to be relational, provenance-sensitive, or otherwise outside that finite descended package. That is exactly the right big-picture conclusion.  

The strongest genuinely new ingredient from the other summaries, in my view, is the cancellation-chart correction. Near a close bad two-point core on a good patch, the correct local base locus is not the naive diagonal, but the collision-cancellation locus
\[
\delta=h_2-h_1=0,\qquad \lambda=-a_2/a_1=1,
\]
and after blow-up the right first-order source datum is the projective direction
\[
\Theta_{m,\theta}=\cos\theta\,D_m+\sin\theta\,D_m'.
\]
That is a real conceptual cleanup. It means some earlier merger-style formulations were aimed at the wrong local chart. It also gives a much sharper theorem target: not “one more diagonal factorization lemma,” but a blow-up functoriality theorem for corrected cubic/quintic witnesses on the cancellation chart. 

I also think the good-patch theorem target in the first summary is very strong. If the corrected cubic/quintic witnesses linearize on the cancellation blow-up to the one-pair functionals
\[
C(m,\theta)=\cos\theta\,c(m)+\sin\theta\,c'(m),
\]
\[
K(m,\theta)=\cos\theta\,A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m)+\sin\theta\,(A_5^{\mathfrak f})'(m),
\]
then on
\[
J\Subset \{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\},
\qquad
M=c(A_5^{\mathfrak f})'-c' A_5^{\mathfrak f},
\]
the unique cubic-killing direction is already quintic-nonzero, so close cancelling bad cores are locally excluded. That is a very clean local theorem target, and it gives a crisp division of labor: on good patches, septic is no longer the first local obstruction if this blow-up linearization lands. 

The second summary pushes the residual-corner side further by broadening the harmless class. It is not just “state-local in finitely many descended transport coordinates” that is safe. It argues that any finite analytic swap-invariant local scalar built from the descended transport state, the amplitude ratio, and symmetric local relational variables is also automatically even and hence \(O((h_1-h_2)^2)\), and then gives the strongest normal form in the
\[
\nu=\log\Lambda,\qquad \Lambda=-a_2/a_1
\]
chart:
\[
F(\nu,\delta,Y)=G(\nu^2,\nu\delta,\delta^2,Y).
\]
That is a very attractive normal-form statement. If it is right as stated for the actual class of local scalars the paper cares about, it is a big gain: it would mean that no ordinary analytic swap-invariant local scalar can keep the residual corner alive. 

The place I would be a little careful is exactly there. The conclusion is powerful, but it is only as good as the hypothesis that the actual corrected quantities really are analytic in that \((\nu,\delta)\) chart across the collision point, rather than merely projectively well-defined after blow-up or defined only modulo some quotienting. So I think the mathematical content is excellent, but in the paper we should present it as a conditional normal-form theorem unless we have already checked that the corrected-block constructions genuinely live in that analytic category. Otherwise it risks sounding more closed than it is. 

So my synthesis now is:

The two-point frontier has separated very cleanly.

On the residual exact fixed-shear corner, the local geometry is now highly rigid: quotient-diagonal, rank-one finite transport state, no hidden finite-order reset, and plausibly no analytic swap-invariant local scalar obstruction either. That strongly suggests the remaining obstruction there, if any, must be non-analytic in the collision chart, genuinely projective/blow-up-direction dependent without analytic extension, provenance-sensitive, discrete, or otherwise package-level exotic. 

On good patches \(J\Subset\{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\}\), the sharpest live theorem target is now the blow-up cubic/quintic functoriality theorem. If that lands, it should kill close cancelling bad cores locally already at quintic order. 

And globally / strongly, order \(7\) still matters, but only through the honest quotient-septic datum
\[
[A_7^{\mathfrak f}]\in \mathfrak f/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f},
\]
so the right theorem target is same reduced image germ or collision-functoriality, not raw septic equality. turn12file1

My current recommendation is to treat the first summary’s blow-up cubic/quintic theorem as the sharpest next local target, and the second summary’s \((\nu,\delta)\) normal form as the strongest residual-corner structural theorem to import, but stated carefully as conditional on genuine analyticity of the corrected local scalar class.
