## Assistant (2026-04-21 20:39:26)

_Thought for 6s_

I think there is one more worthwhile compression, and it sharpens the fixed-shear endgame into a very concrete fork.

The previous step reduced strict three-lobe excess to a separated same-tower translation symmetry, provided the transport-curvature observable
\[
\Xi(u):=\frac{\widehat{\mathcal D}'(u)}{\widehat{\mathcal D}(u)^3}
\]
is single-valued over \(q=\widehat Q(u)\). The next thing to notice is that this “single-valued over \(\widehat Q\)” condition itself has an exact differential meaning.

Write
\[
\widehat{\mathcal D}=\widehat Q',
\qquad
\Xi=\frac{\widehat Q''}{(\widehat Q')^3}.
\]
Now compute
\[
\frac{d}{du}\Bigl(\frac{1}{(\widehat Q')^2}\Bigr)
=
-2\,\frac{\widehat Q''}{(\widehat Q')^3}
=
-2\Xi(u).
\]
So if \(\Xi(u)=F(\widehat Q(u))\), then
\[
\frac{d}{du}\Bigl(\frac{1}{(\widehat Q')^2}\Bigr)
=
-2F(\widehat Q(u)).
\]
Because \(d\widehat Q/du=\widehat Q'\), this is equivalent, on each monotone run, to saying that
\[
\frac{d}{d\widehat Q}\Bigl(\frac{1}{\widehat Q'}\Bigr)
=
-\frac{\widehat Q''}{(\widehat Q')^3}
=
-\Xi(u)
\]
is a function of \(\widehat Q\) alone. In other words, the reciprocal slope profile
\[
R(q):=\frac{1}{\widehat{\mathcal D}(\phi(q))}
\]
on any monotone branch solves a scalar first-order ODE depending only on \(q\).

That was the mechanism behind the constant-gap conclusion. But now we can package it more cleanly:

\[
\boxed{
\Xi=F(\widehat Q)\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
\frac{1}{\widehat Q'} \text{ is, branchwise, an affine primitive in the value variable }q=\widehat Q.
}
\]

So the live strict-excess case is now controlled by a very concrete “integrability in value space” question.

That gives a sharper fork than before.

## 1. Exact value-space integrability fork

On the quotient-visible fixed-shear branch, exactly one of the following must happen.

First possibility: the reciprocal slope \(1/\widehat Q'\) is integrable as a function of the value variable \(q=\widehat Q\), i.e. \(\Xi=F(\widehat Q)\). Then, as shown last turn, strict excess forces the two outer reciprocal-slope profiles to satisfy the same scalar ODE on the overlap interval, so their difference is constant. Since strict excess also forces an interior zero of that difference, it vanishes identically, and therefore the same-value transport map has constant gap:
\[
\phi_2(q)-\phi_0(q)\equiv C.
\]
Equivalently,
\[
\widehat Q(u+C)=\widehat Q(u)
\]
on an open interval, hence all higher derivatives agree there too. So strict excess collapses to an open local translation symmetry of the entire explicit quotient-visible tower.

Second possibility: \(\Xi\) is **not** single-valued over \(\widehat Q\). Then the first genuinely new fixed-shear obstruction has been identified very concretely: it is exactly the failure of value-space integrability for reciprocal slope. That is no longer an abstract “nonlocal transport issue”; it is a specific transport non-integrability phenomenon.

This is a real improvement, because the endgame is no longer “prove or disprove some inequality in the run amplitudes.” It is:

- either prove value-space integrability and then kill the resulting translation symmetry,
- or show that the first real obstruction is failure of value-space integrability itself.

That matches the updated paper’s conclusion that the remaining fixed-shear issue is nonlocal transport, not a new pointwise generator.

## 2. A new canonical observable

There is also a cleaner canonical quantity than \(\Xi\) itself. Define
\[
\Psi(u):=\frac{1}{(\widehat Q'(u))^2}=\frac{1}{\widehat{\mathcal D}(u)^2}.
\]
Then
\[
\Psi'(u)=-2\Xi(u).
\]
So the condition \(\Xi=F(\widehat Q)\) is equivalent to
\[
\Psi'(u)=G(\widehat Q(u))
\]
for some scalar \(G\). On a monotone run, that can be rewritten as
\[
\frac{d\Psi}{d\widehat Q}
=
\frac{\Psi'(u)}{\widehat Q'(u)}
=
\frac{G(\widehat Q(u))}{\widehat Q'(u)},
\]
but the most useful form is still: the derivative of \(\Psi\) along the transport direction depends only on the value coordinate.

Why is this helpful? Because \(\Psi\) is even more symmetric than \(1/\widehat Q'\), and the strict-excess crossing is equivalently a crossing of the square roots of \(\Psi\). So one possible theorem target is not directly about \(\Xi\), but about the branchwise dependence of \(\Psi\) on \(\widehat Q\).

A clean target would be:

> on separated outer runs of the actual RH quotient-visible fixed-shear branch, the function \(\Psi=1/\widehat{\mathcal D}^2\) is single-valued over \(\widehat Q\).

That is equivalent to saying the two outer runs determine the same reciprocal-slope-square profile in value space. If true, strict excess again collapses to constant-gap transport and hence local translation symmetry.

## 3. Why this is closer to the generator audit

This fork is, I think, better aligned with the updated generator audit than my previous phrasing.

The audit says: no second primitive pointwise highest-new generator has appeared in the explicit package. So the remaining obstruction should not be sought as one more local field. Here, the branchwise single-valuedness of \(\Xi\) or \(\Psi\) over \(\widehat Q\) is not introducing a new field at all. It is asking whether an already explicit differential expression descends to value space. That is exactly the kind of nonlocal transport statement that still could matter after the pointwise generator audit. It uses the existing tower rather than extending it.

So the live fixed-shear endgame is now naturally phrased as:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Does } \frac{\widehat Q''}{(\widehat Q')^3}
\text{ descend to a single-valued function of } \widehat Q
\text{ across separated outer runs?}
}
\]

If yes, strict excess forces translation symmetry.
If no, that descent failure itself is the first genuinely nontrivial transport obstruction.

That is a much more canonical fork.

## 4. Translation symmetry can be weakened further

There is also a useful weakening of the constant-gap conclusion.

If the reciprocal-slope gap is constant and has an interior zero, then the same-value transport map \(T\) satisfies
\[
T'(u)\equiv 1
\]
on the overlap interval, not just at one point. Indeed,
\[
T'(u)=\frac{\widehat{\mathcal D}(u)}{\widehat{\mathcal D}(T(u))},
\]
and equality of reciprocal slopes along the overlap gives equality of \(\widehat{\mathcal D}\), hence \(T'\equiv 1\).

So strict excess plus value-space integrability implies the same-value transport is an affine map
\[
T(u)=u+C.
\]

This is slightly stronger than the earlier constant-gap statement, because it says the transport correspondence itself is affine, not just that the inverse-branch difference is constant. So the final contradiction target could be formulated as:

> rule out nontrivial affine same-value transport between separated outer runs of the quotient-visible fixed-shear branch.

That may be more natural than speaking of “translation symmetry of the full tower,” though mathematically it is the same.

## 5. Best next theorem targets

I think the sharpest remaining theorem targets in this lane are now:

### Target A: value-space integrability theorem
Show that on separated outer runs of the actual RH quotient-visible fixed-shear branch,
\[
\Xi(u)=\frac{\widehat Q''(u)}{(\widehat Q'(u))^3}
\]
is single-valued over \(q=\widehat Q(u)\).

Then strict excess implies affine same-value transport \(T(u)=u+C\).

### Target B: no affine same-value transport theorem
Show there is no nonzero constant \(C\) and open interval \(U\) such that
\[
\widehat Q(u+C)=\widehat Q(u)
\qquad(u\in U)
\]
between separated outer runs.

If both land, the strict three-lobe case is dead.

A weaker alternative would be:

### Target C: non-integrability is the first obstruction
If \(\Xi\) fails to be single-valued over \(\widehat Q\), identify that failure explicitly as the first genuine nonlocal fixed-shear transport obstruction, so the proof frontier becomes exact rather than diffuse.

## 6. Strongest new structural finding

The strongest new structural conclusion from this round is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The live fixed-shear strict-excess case is now reduced to an exact value-space integrability fork for the reciprocal-slope transport.}
}
\]

That is better than an amplitude inequality, better than a generic jet-self-intersection statement, and better than “some nonlocal transport issue.” It says precisely what the remaining obstruction must be.

So my current best mathematical summary is:

- equality \(B_1=B_0+B_2\) is sterile;
- strict excess \(B_1>B_0+B_2\) yields open same-value transport;
- if reciprocal-slope transport is value-space integrable, that transport is affine and hence gives a separated local translation symmetry of the quotient-visible tower;
- if it is not value-space integrable, that failure is itself the first concrete nonlocal fixed-shear obstruction.

That is the sharpest continuation I can see.

## Assistant (2026-04-21 21:03:59)

_Thought for 17s_

I think there is one more real step, and it improves the fixed-shear lane a lot.

The new point is: if the strict-excess case ever reaches the “affine same-value transport” stage, then analyticity upgrades that from a local coincidence to a **genuine local periodicity**, and that is incompatible with the already-compressed three-run model.

So the strict-excess lane now reduces to an even sharper fork:

- either value-space integrability fails, and that failure is the first genuine nonlocal transport obstruction;
- or value-space integrability holds, in which case strict excess forces local periodicity of \(\widehat Q\), which should be impossible in the three-run quotient-visible setting.

That is stronger than the previous “same-tower translation symmetry” phrasing.

---

## 1. Start from the previous reduction

We are on the quotient-visible exact fixed-shear branch, downstairs in
\[
u=t^2,
\qquad
\widehat{\mathcal D}(u)=\widehat Q'(u).
\]

In the only live three-run case, strict excess
\[
B_1>B_0+B_2
\]
gives an open same-value transport between the two outer runs. If, in addition, the transport-curvature observable
\[
\Xi(u):=\frac{\widehat Q''(u)}{(\widehat Q'(u))^3}
\]
is single-valued over \(q=\widehat Q(u)\), then the reciprocal-slope profiles satisfy the same scalar ODE in \(q\), so their gap is constant. Since strict excess also forces an interior zero of that gap, the gap vanishes identically. Equivalently, the same-value transport is affine:
\[
T(u)=u+C
\]
on an open interval, with \(C\neq 0\), and therefore
\[
\widehat Q(u+C)=\widehat Q(u)
\]
there.

That was the previous reduction.

---

## 2. Analyticity upgrades affine transport to local periodicity

Now define
\[
F(u):=\widehat Q(u+C)-\widehat Q(u).
\]
This is analytic on the intersection of the branch domain with its translate by \(-C\). If \(F\) vanishes on a nonempty open interval \(U\), then by the identity theorem
\[
F\equiv 0
\]
on the whole connected component of that overlap containing \(U\).

So the affine same-value transport is not just a one-off local relation. It forces genuine local periodicity:
\[
\widehat Q(u+C)=\widehat Q(u),
\qquad
\widehat{\mathcal D}(u+C)=\widehat{\mathcal D}(u)
\]
throughout the whole connected overlap component.

In particular, every derivative agrees:
\[
\widehat Q^{(k)}(u+C)=\widehat Q^{(k)}(u)
\qquad(k\ge 0).
\]

So strict excess plus value-space integrability gives an honest local period \(C\) of the full quotient jet.

That is already a much stronger obstruction.

---

## 3. Why this clashes with the three-run compression

The updated paper’s fixed-shear reduction says that, in the quotient-visible model, no-reentry compresses the live global data to at most three sign-runs of
\[
\widehat{\mathcal D}=\widehat Q'.
\]
The strict case is exactly the three-run case.

But if
\[
\widehat{\mathcal D}(u+C)=\widehat{\mathcal D}(u)
\]
on an open connected overlap, then the sign pattern and the zero pattern of \(\widehat{\mathcal D}\) repeat with period \(C\) across that overlap. In particular:

- critical points translate to critical points,
- extrema of \(\widehat Q\) translate to extrema of the same type,
- and the sign-run pattern reproduces itself.

That is fundamentally a periodic-type structure. A genuine three-run compressed model is the opposite: it is a finite excursion structure with one central run and two outer runs, not a repeating pattern.

So the local periodicity forced by strict excess is already strongly at odds with the finite three-run geometry.

At the very least, it says the strict case cannot remain an isolated three-lobe event. It would propagate a copy of the same lobe structure under translation.

That is the key qualitative contradiction.

---

## 4. A more explicit contradiction mechanism

Let the three runs be \(J_0,J_1,J_2\), with \(J_0\) and \(J_2\) the outer runs involved in the strict-excess overlap. The affine transport identifies an open subinterval of \(J_0\) with an open subinterval of \(J_2\) by
\[
u\mapsto u+C.
\]
Since \(\widehat Q'\) also agrees under this translation, the local sign of \(\widehat{\mathcal D}\) is preserved. So the translated piece of \(J_0\) sits inside a run of the same sign as \(J_0\), which is exactly why it lands in \(J_2\).

Now extend by analyticity on the overlap component. The translated critical endpoint of \(J_0\) must map to a critical point of the same type near the endpoint of \(J_2\). But then the translated adjacent sign-change structure also reproduces. In other words, the translated local run decomposition of \(J_0\cup J_1\) begins to recreate another copy of the two-sign-change pattern next to \(J_2\).

That is incompatible with the statement that the quotient-visible branch has at most three sign-runs globally. Periodic continuation would force further repeated structure beyond the compressed three-run model.

So the contradiction is not merely “periodicity feels wrong.” It is:

> local periodicity of \(\widehat{\mathcal D}\) forces replication of the sign-run pattern, whereas the quotient-visible no-reentry theorem has already compressed the branch to a finite three-run configuration.

That is the right conflict.

---

## 5. Clean theorem candidate

This suggests the next theorem:

### No local periodicity theorem
On the actual quotient-visible exact fixed-shear branch in the compressed three-run regime, there is no nonzero constant \(C\) and nonempty open interval \(U\) such that
\[
\widehat Q(u+C)=\widehat Q(u)
\qquad(u\in U).
\]

Equivalently, there is no nontrivial local period of \(\widehat Q\), or of \(\widehat{\mathcal D}\).

If this theorem holds, then the strict-excess case is impossible whenever the value-space integrability condition \(\Xi=F(\widehat Q)\) holds.

This is cleaner than the previous “same-tower translation symmetry” statement, because it uses only \(\widehat Q\) itself and immediately propagates by analyticity.

---

## 6. So the fixed-shear lane is now a very sharp fork

The whole strict three-run fixed-shear obstruction now reduces to:

### Fork A: value-space integrability holds
There exists \(F\) with
\[
\Xi(u)=\frac{\widehat Q''(u)}{(\widehat Q'(u))^3}=F(\widehat Q(u))
\]
across the two outer runs.

Then strict excess forces affine same-value transport, hence local periodicity of \(\widehat Q\), which should be excluded by the finite three-run compression.

### Fork B: value-space integrability fails
Then that failure is the first concrete nonlocal fixed-shear transport obstruction.

This is now much more precise than “some nonlocal transport issue remains.”

---

## 7. One more useful reformulation

There is also a neat equivalent form.

Because
\[
\widehat Q(u+C)=\widehat Q(u)
\]
implies
\[
\widehat Q'(u+C)=\widehat Q'(u),
\]
the local period \(C\) makes the quotient jet map
\[
u\mapsto (\widehat Q(u),\widehat Q'(u))
\]
non-injective on an open family. But earlier we reduced strict excess to a self-intersection of the reciprocal-slope jet
\[
u\mapsto \left(\widehat Q(u),\frac1{\widehat Q'(u)}\right).
\]
So under value-space integrability, a single jet self-intersection bootstraps to an **open family** of jet coincidences. That is much more rigid than a one-time crossing.

So another strong theorem target is:

### No open jet coincidence theorem
The quotient jet map
\[
u\mapsto (\widehat Q(u),\widehat Q'(u))
\]
cannot have an open one-parameter coincidence family between separated outer runs.

That is equivalent to excluding the periodicity conclusion.

---

## 8. Strongest new structural finding

The strongest new structural conclusion from this round is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Under value-space integrability of } \Xi,\ \text{strict three-lobe excess does not merely force a pointwise jet coincidence; it forces open local periodicity of the quotient transport branch.}
}
\]

That is a much sharper contradiction candidate than the original amplitude inequality.

So the mixed fixed-shear lane is now really down to:

- prove value-space integrability of \(\Xi\), and then exclude local periodicity;
- or else identify failure of value-space integrability as the first genuine remaining fixed-shear obstruction.

That is the sharpest continuation I can see.
## User (2026-04-21 21:38:22)

## Assistant (2026-04-21 21:39:43)

_Thought for 1m 12s_

I think this finally gives a real closure mechanism for the strict three-lobe lane, conditional only on the value-space integrability step.

The key new point is:

if strict excess ever reaches the affine same-value transport stage
\[
\widehat Q(u+C)=\widehat Q(u)
\]
between the two outer runs, then analyticity does not just give a local coincidence. It propagates the **adjacent sign-run structure** across the critical endpoints, and that is incompatible with the already-proved “at most three runs” compression.

So the strict-excess case is now reduced to a very sharp theorem pair.

---

## 1. Recall the previous reduction

On the quotient-visible exact fixed-shear branch, in the only live three-run case, strict excess
\[
B_1>B_0+B_2
\]
gives an open same-value transport between the two outer runs \(J_0,J_2\).

If, moreover, the transport-curvature observable
\[
\Xi(u):=\frac{\widehat Q''(u)}{(\widehat Q'(u))^3}
\]
is single-valued over \(q=\widehat Q(u)\), then the reciprocal-slope profiles on the two outer runs satisfy the same scalar ODE in \(q\), so their gap is constant. Since strict excess also forces that gap to vanish somewhere, it vanishes identically. Hence the same-value transport is affine:
\[
T(u)=u+C
\]
for some nonzero constant \(C\), and on an open interval \(U\subset J_0\),
\[
\widehat Q(u+C)=\widehat Q(u).
\]

That was the previous endpoint.

---

## 2. Analytic continuation upgrades this to full-run transport

Define
\[
F(u):=\widehat Q(u+C)-\widehat Q(u).
\]
This is analytic wherever both \(u\) and \(u+C\) lie in the quotient-branch domain.

If \(F\) vanishes on a nonempty open interval \(U\subset J_0\), then by the identity theorem it vanishes on the whole connected overlap component of the shifted domain containing \(U\).

Now let
\[
J_0=(a,b),\qquad J_2=(a+C,b+C)
\]
be the two outer runs after relabeling by the same transport constant \(C\). Why must the endpoints match this way?

Because if, say, \(b+C\) were an interior point of \(J_2\), then from
\[
\widehat Q'(u+C)=\widehat Q'(u)
\]
and the fact that \(\widehat Q'(u)\to 0\) as \(u\uparrow b\) (since \(b\) is a critical endpoint of \(J_0\)), we would get
\[
\widehat Q'(b+C)=0,
\]
which would make \(b+C\) an interior critical point of the monotone run \(J_2\), impossible. So endpoints must map to endpoints.

Thus the affine transport identifies the **entire outer run** \(J_0\) with the entire outer run \(J_2\).

That is already much stronger than an arbitrary local overlap.

---

## 3. Propagation across the critical endpoints

Now comes the crucial step.

Since \(F\) is analytic and vanishes on \(J_0\), it vanishes in a neighborhood of each endpoint \(a\) and \(b\) as long as the shifted points \(a+C\), \(b+C\) stay in the local quotient-branch domain. But they do: these are exactly the critical endpoints of \(J_2\), and the quotient branch is analytic across critical points.

Therefore
\[
\widehat Q(u+C)=\widehat Q(u)
\]
holds not only on \(J_0\), but in small neighborhoods crossing the endpoints \(a\) and \(b\).

Differentiating,
\[
\widehat Q'(u+C)=\widehat Q'(u)
\]
in those neighborhoods too.

So the sign pattern of \(\widehat{\mathcal D}=\widehat Q'\) adjacent to \(J_0\) is copied adjacent to \(J_2\).

But adjacent to \(J_0\), one sees the middle run \(J_1\), on which \(\widehat{\mathcal D}\) has the opposite sign. Therefore the translation by \(C\) forces an interval immediately adjacent to \(J_2\) with that same opposite sign.

In other words, the middle-run sign pattern next to \(J_0\) is reproduced next to \(J_2\).

That creates a **fourth sign-run** beyond \(J_2\).

And that is impossible, because the updated fixed-shear reduction already proves that the quotient-visible no-reentry branch has at most three sign-runs. turn15file1

So we get:

\[
\boxed{
\text{A nontrivial affine same-value transport between the two outer runs is incompatible with the three-run quotient-visible compression.}
}
\]

This is the missing contradiction.

---

## 4. Clean theorem statement

Here is the theorem candidate in clean form.

### No affine outer-run transport theorem
Let \(J_0,J_1,J_2\) be the three sign-runs of \(\widehat{\mathcal D}=\widehat Q'\) on a quotient-visible exact fixed-shear branch. Then there do not exist a nonzero constant \(C\) and an open interval \(U\subset J_0\) such that
\[
\widehat Q(u+C)=\widehat Q(u)
\qquad (u\in U),
\]
with \(U+C\subset J_2\).

#### Proof sketch
Analytic continuation upgrades the equality from \(U\) to the full outer run \(J_0\), hence to neighborhoods crossing its critical endpoints. Differentiating shows the adjacent sign pattern of \(\widehat Q'\) next to \(J_0\) is copied next to \(J_2\), producing another sign-run beyond \(J_2\). That contradicts the “at most three sign-runs” theorem. ∎

---

## 5. Consequence for the strict three-lobe case

Combine this with the previous reduction.

If the transport-curvature observable
\[
\Xi(u)=\frac{\widehat Q''(u)}{(\widehat Q'(u))^3}
\]
is single-valued over \(q=\widehat Q(u)\) across the two outer runs, then strict excess
\[
B_1>B_0+B_2
\]
forces affine same-value transport, which is impossible by the theorem above.

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\Xi=F(\widehat Q)\ \text{ across outer runs } \Longrightarrow\ B_1>B_0+B_2\ \text{ is impossible.}
}
\]

Since equality
\[
B_1=B_0+B_2
\]
was already reduced to sterile touching, this would close the three-run quotient-visible fixed-shear lane completely.

---

## 6. What remains now

So the fixed-shear lane is now down to an extremely sharp fork:

### Route A
Prove the value-space integrability statement
\[
\Xi(u)=\frac{\widehat Q''(u)}{(\widehat Q'(u))^3}=F(\widehat Q(u))
\]
across separated outer runs.

Then strict excess is impossible by the affine-transport contradiction above.

### Route B
If this fails, then the failure of \(\Xi\) to descend to value space is itself the first genuine nonlocal fixed-shear transport obstruction.

That is no longer vague. It is an exact statement about branchwise non-single-valuedness of the transport-curvature observable.

---

## 7. Strongest new structural finding

The strongest new structural conclusion from this round is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Under value-space integrability of } \Xi,\ \text{strict three-lobe excess propagates by analyticity to a forbidden replication of the sign-run pattern.}
}
\]

So the strict-excess case is no longer just “some amplitude imbalance.” It has been reduced to a local periodicity/replication mechanism that directly clashes with the finite three-run theorem already in the paper.

That is, I think, the sharpest continuation available right now.

## Assistant (2026-04-21 21:41:09)

I’m pushing on the remaining fixed-shear fork directly now: whether the “value-space integrability” condition can be reformulated in a more intrinsic way using the inverse branches of \(\widehat Q\), rather than as an ad hoc condition on \(\Xi\).

_Thought for 5s_

I think the next real step is to rewrite the value-space integrability condition in a way that makes the remaining fork more intrinsic and easier to attack.

Right now the fork is:

- either
  \[
  \Xi(u):=\frac{\widehat Q''(u)}{(\widehat Q'(u))^3}
  \]
  is single-valued over \(q=\widehat Q(u)\) across the two outer runs, in which case strict excess forces affine same-value transport and then forbidden run-pattern replication;
- or \(\Xi\) is not single-valued over \(\widehat Q\), and that failure is the first genuine nonlocal fixed-shear obstruction.

The new point is that \(\Xi\) is not an arbitrary expression. It is exactly the second derivative of the inverse branches of \(\widehat Q\) in the value variable.

That gives a much cleaner formulation.

---

## 1. Inverse-branch calculus

On any monotone run \(J\) of the quotient-visible fixed-shear branch, let
\[
\phi:\widehat Q(J)\to J
\]
be the inverse branch of \(\widehat Q\). Then
\[
\phi'(q)=\frac{1}{\widehat Q'(\phi(q))}=\frac{1}{\widehat{\mathcal D}(\phi(q))}.
\]
Differentiating once more,
\[
\phi''(q)
=
-\frac{\widehat Q''(\phi(q))}{(\widehat Q'(\phi(q)))^3}
=
-\Xi(\phi(q)).
\]

So on each run, the observable \(\Xi\) is exactly the negative second derivative of the inverse branch in value space.

In particular, on the two outer runs \(J_0,J_2\) with inverse branches \(\phi_0,\phi_2\), we have
\[
\phi_0''(q)=-\Xi(\phi_0(q)),
\qquad
\phi_2''(q)=-\Xi(\phi_2(q)).
\]

Thus the single-valuedness condition
\[
\Xi(u)=F(\widehat Q(u))
\]
across the two outer runs is equivalent to
\[
\phi_0''(q)=\phi_2''(q)
\qquad\text{for all }q\text{ in the overlap interval } \mathcal I.
\]

That is a much more natural statement.

---

## 2. The outer inverse branches differ by an affine function

If
\[
\phi_0''(q)=\phi_2''(q)
\]
on \(\mathcal I\), then their difference
\[
\Delta(q):=\phi_2(q)-\phi_0(q)
\]
satisfies
\[
\Delta''(q)=0.
\]
So
\[
\Delta(q)=Aq+B
\]
is affine in \(q\).

This is stronger and cleaner than the earlier gap analysis.

Now recall that in the strict-excess case, \(\Delta'(q)\) must vanish somewhere in the interior of \(\mathcal I\), because the reciprocal-slope gap changes sign at the two ends. But
\[
\Delta'(q)=\phi_2'(q)-\phi_0'(q).
\]
So if \(\Delta\) is affine and \(\Delta'(q_*)=0\) at one interior point \(q_*\), then \(\Delta'\equiv 0\) on all of \(\mathcal I\). Hence \(\Delta\) is constant:
\[
\phi_2(q)-\phi_0(q)\equiv C.
\]

So the previous constant-gap conclusion now comes from a very clean mechanism:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Single-valuedness of }\Xi
\iff
\phi_0''=\phi_2''
\iff
\phi_2-\phi_0 \text{ is affine in }q.
}
\]
And strict excess forces that affine function to have zero slope, hence be constant.

This is a much sharper reduction than working directly with \(\Gamma\).

---

## 3. A new geometric interpretation: equal inverse curvature

The quantity \(\phi''\) is the curvature of the inverse branch in value space. So the condition that \(\Xi\) be single-valued over \(\widehat Q\) means:

> at equal \(q\)-value, the two outer inverse branches have the same inverse curvature.

Then strict excess plus the sign change of the reciprocal-slope gap forces these two inverse branches not only to have equal curvature, but to differ by a constant translation.

So the strict-excess obstruction can now be phrased entirely in value-space inverse-branch geometry:

\[
\boxed{
\text{If the two outer inverse branches have the same second derivative as functions of }q,
\text{ then strict excess forces them to be translates.}
}
\]

That is a very clean theorem target.

---

## 4. The remaining fork becomes even sharper

So the fixed-shear endgame is now:

### Route A: inverse-curvature matching
On separated outer runs,
\[
\phi_0''(q)=\phi_2''(q)
\]
on their common value interval.

Then strict excess forces
\[
\phi_2(q)=\phi_0(q)+C,
\]
hence
\[
\widehat Q(u+C)=\widehat Q(u)
\]
on an open interval, and by the previous round this propagates to a forbidden replication of the sign-run pattern, contradicting the three-run compression. turn15file1

### Route B: inverse-curvature mismatch
The two outer inverse branches do **not** have the same second derivative at equal value \(q\). Then the first genuine nonlocal fixed-shear obstruction has an exact form:
\[
\phi_0''(q)-\phi_2''(q)\neq 0
\]
somewhere on the overlap interval.

This is better than saying vaguely “\(\Xi\) is not single-valued over \(\widehat Q\).” It says the obstruction is exactly a failure of inverse-curvature matching between separated outer runs.

That is a much more geometric statement.

---

## 5. A canonical gap observable

This also gives a more canonical gap than \(\Gamma\). Define
\[
\Delta(q):=\phi_2(q)-\phi_0(q).
\]
Then
\[
\Delta'(q)=\frac{1}{\widehat{\mathcal D}(\phi_2(q))}-\frac{1}{\widehat{\mathcal D}(\phi_0(q))},
\]
which is the reciprocal-slope gap from before, and
\[
\Delta''(q)=\phi_2''(q)-\phi_0''(q)
=
-\Xi(\phi_2(q))+\Xi(\phi_0(q)).
\]

So:

- strict excess forces an interior zero of \(\Delta'\);
- value-space integrability is exactly \(\Delta''=0\);
- then \(\Delta\) is affine, and the interior zero of \(\Delta'\) forces \(\Delta\) to be constant.

This is the cleanest one-variable package yet.

So the final mixed fixed-shear problem is now a question about the second derivative of the inverse-branch gap \(\Delta\).

---

## 6. Strongest new theorem target

The sharpest theorem target I see now is:

### Inverse-curvature separation theorem
On the actual RH quotient-visible exact fixed-shear branch, for any separated outer runs with common value interval \(\mathcal I\), the inverse-branch gap
\[
\Delta(q)=\phi_2(q)-\phi_0(q)
\]
satisfies either:

- \(\Delta''(q)\equiv 0\), in which case strict excess would force \(\Delta\) constant and hence forbidden local periodicity;
- or \(\Delta''\) has definite sign / one-sign behavior, preventing the interior critical point of \(\Delta\) that strict excess requires.

A slightly weaker but still decisive version is just:

### No interior critical point theorem for the inverse gap
The inverse-branch gap \(\Delta(q)\) has no interior critical point on \(\mathcal I\).

Because strict excess is equivalent to exactly such a critical point.

This is even sharper than the reciprocal-slope-gap formulation, because it packages everything into the geometry of one scalar function \(\Delta\).

---

## 7. Why this feels like the right endpoint

This matches the updated paper remarkably well.

On the nonmixed/global side, the endgame is a one-variable zero problem for endpoint-gap functions. On the fixed-shear quotient side, the endgame is now also a one-variable critical-point problem, but for the inverse-branch gap
\[
\Delta(q)=\phi_2(q)-\phi_0(q).
\]

So both remaining lanes are now compressed to gap-function control, just in different coordinates:

- affine endpoint-space on the nonmixed side;
- value-space inverse-branch geometry on the fixed-shear side.

That is a very satisfying convergence.

---

## 8. Bottom line

The strongest continuation from this round is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The strict three-lobe fixed-shear obstruction is now equivalent to an interior critical point of the inverse-branch gap }
\Delta(q)=\phi_2(q)-\phi_0(q).
}
\]

Moreover,

- \(\Delta''=0\) is exactly the value-space integrability condition for the reciprocal-slope transport;
- under that condition, strict excess forces \(\Delta\) to be constant, hence forbidden local periodicity;
- if \(\Delta''\neq 0\), then that curvature mismatch is itself the first concrete nonlocal fixed-shear obstruction.

So the fixed-shear endgame has now been reduced to the cleanest possible fork I can see:

1. prove \(\Delta''=0\) and then rule out constant \(\Delta\) by three-run compression; or
2. identify and control the sign/variation of \(\Delta''\) directly to rule out interior critical points of \(\Delta\).

That is the sharpest math attack I can see right now.

## Assistant (2026-04-21 21:47:23)

_Thought for a few seconds_

Here is the full handback of the attack and where it stands now.

The shortest honest summary is this:

the mixed fixed-shear lane has been compressed from a vague residual branch problem to a very specific **quotient-visible transport problem downstairs in \(u=t^2\)**. The only genuinely live quotient-visible obstruction now appears in the **strict three-run lobe-excess case**
\[
B_1>B_0+B_2,
\]
and even that has been reduced several times: first to open same-value transport between the two outer runs, then to a jet self-intersection, then to a reciprocal-slope crossing, and finally to an interior critical point of a one-variable inverse-branch gap function. Equality
\[
B_1=B_0+B_2
\]
has been reduced to sterile touching. The quartic–sextic rung is inert for this lobe-amplitude obstruction. The main remaining fork is now: either a certain value-space transport integrability holds and strict excess forces forbidden local periodicity / run-pattern replication, or that integrability fails and the failure itself is the first concrete nonlocal fixed-shear obstruction. This is well aligned with the updated paper’s conclusion that no second pointwise highest-new generator has appeared and that the remaining burden is nonlocal transport, not new local algebra. turn15file1

I’ll write this in a more complete theorem-style summary.

---

## 1. Starting point from the updated paper

The derivative-geometry updates changed the landscape in three big ways.

On the nonmixed/global affine side, the remaining burden is now remote endpoint/branch incidence, encoded by monotone endpoint-gap functions \(G_{\xi,J}\). Pure affine/pseudoline/interval-graph geometry has reached its ceiling; any final closure there must use RH-specific structure. 

On the exact fixed-shear side, the paper now has the right quotient-visible reduction: repeated pairs are exactly the involutive pairs \(t\leftrightarrow -t\); downstairs the real transport data are \(\widehat Q\) and \(\widehat{\mathcal D}=\widehat Q'\); the live combinatorics compress to sign-run amplitudes \(B_j\); there are at most three sign-runs on a quotient-visible no-reentry branch; the only surviving three-run condition is
\[
B_1\ge B_0+B_2;
\]
strict inequality gives real overlap, equality gives only critical-value touching; and the quartic–sextic rung is inert because \(\widehat{\mathcal D}(0)\neq 0\). 

On the highest-new side, the explicit pointwise package has been audited and no second primitive pointwise highest-new generator has appeared beyond the current tower headed by \(r=q^{(7)}\). So any remaining fixed-shear obstruction should be thought of as a **nonlocal transport phenomenon**, not as one more local pointwise field. 

That is the context in which the rest of the attack happened.

---

## 2. The fixed-shear lane was reformulated as a quotient-visible problem

The first major compression is conceptual.

Instead of treating the mixed residual lane as another local branch-classification problem, I treated it as a quotient-visible transport problem downstairs in
\[
u=t^2.
\]
The involutive upstairs pairing \(t\leftrightarrow -t\) means all nontrivial residual repeated-pair issues should be studied downstairs in the quotient branch via the scalar
\[
\widehat Q(u),\qquad \widehat{\mathcal D}(u)=\widehat Q'(u).
\]

That lines up with the updated paper’s current formulation. It also demotes some of my earlier cancellation-chart first-jet work: those local jet arguments are still useful as side structure, but they are no longer the main endgame. The paper has moved the fixed-shear problem downstairs into quotient transport.

That was the first strategic correction.

---

## 3. Equality \(B_1=B_0+B_2\) was reduced to sterile touching

The first concrete theorem-level gain on the fixed-shear side was the treatment of the equality case.

Suppose we are in the quotient-visible three-run case. Let \(J_0,J_1,J_2\) be the three sign-runs of \(\widehat{\mathcal D}\), with \(J_0,J_2\) the outer runs. Their images under \(\widehat Q\) are intervals \(I_0,I_1,I_2\). The three-lobe criterion says that equality
\[
B_1=B_0+B_2
\]
means the outer image intervals meet only in a boundary point, not on an open interval.

I sharpened that into a sterility statement:

- downstairs, the equal-value relation between the two outer runs is locally zero-dimensional;
- there is no open value interval supporting a same-value branch;
- lifting back by \(u=t^2\) cannot turn a zero-dimensional quotient coincidence into a genuine local repeated-pair branch upstairs.

So the clean theorem candidate is:

> **Touching-is-sterile theorem.** In the quotient-visible fixed-shear three-run model, equality \(B_1=B_0+B_2\) gives only critical-value touching and cannot support a genuine local repeated-pair branch.

This is not yet inserted as a proved theorem in the paper, but mathematically the mechanism is very clear: equality is only boundary touching, not open overlap.

That is a genuine positive structural gain.

---

## 4. Strict excess \(B_1>B_0+B_2\) was reduced to open same-value transport

Once equality was isolated as sterile, the only live quotient-visible fixed-shear obstruction became strict excess
\[
B_1>B_0+B_2.
\]

The first reduction there was:

> **Strict excess \(\Longleftrightarrow\) open same-value transport between the two outer runs.**

Concretely, strict excess gives an open value interval
\[
\mathcal I\subset \widehat Q(J_0)\cap \widehat Q(J_2)
\]
and inverse branches
\[
\phi_0,\phi_2:\mathcal I\to J_0,J_2
\]
with
\[
\widehat Q(\phi_0(q))=\widehat Q(\phi_2(q))=q.
\]

So the problem ceased to be “an inequality in three numbers” and became “an open analytic same-value correspondence between separated outer runs.”

That was the first major sharpening of the strict-excess case.

---

## 5. Strict excess was then reduced to same-value / same-slope coincidence

From the same-value transport, I studied the \(u\)-gap
\[
G(q):=\phi_2(q)-\phi_0(q).
\]
Differentiating gives
\[
G'(q)=\frac{1}{\widehat{\mathcal D}(\phi_2(q))}-\frac{1}{\widehat{\mathcal D}(\phi_0(q))}.
\]

Endpoint behavior of the outer runs shows that \(G'(q)\) has opposite signs at the two ends of the overlap interval \(\mathcal I\). Therefore \(G'(q)\) has an interior zero. Equivalently, strict excess forces a point \(q_*\in\mathcal I\) such that for \(u_0=\phi_0(q_*)\), \(u_2=\phi_2(q_*)\),
\[
\widehat Q(u_0)=\widehat Q(u_2),
\qquad
\widehat{\mathcal D}(u_0)=\widehat{\mathcal D}(u_2).
\]

So strict excess forces a self-intersection of the quotient jet map
\[
u\mapsto (\widehat Q(u),\widehat{\mathcal D}(u)).
\]

That was a real theorem-level reduction: from an integrated run-amplitude inequality to a pointwise same-value / same-slope coincidence.

---

## 6. This was refined to reciprocal-slope crossing and then to an inverse-branch gap

I then noticed that the more natural transport observable is not \((\widehat Q,\widehat{\mathcal D})\), but rather reciprocal slope.

Define the reciprocal-slope profiles
\[
R_j(q):=\frac{1}{\widehat{\mathcal D}(\phi_j(q))},
\]
and the reciprocal-slope gap
\[
\Gamma(q):=R_2(q)-R_0(q).
\]
Then strict excess forces an interior zero of \(\Gamma\).

This can be packaged more canonically by defining the inverse-branch gap
\[
\Delta(q):=\phi_2(q)-\phi_0(q).
\]
Then
\[
\Delta'(q)=\Gamma(q)
=
\frac{1}{\widehat{\mathcal D}(\phi_2(q))}
-
\frac{1}{\widehat{\mathcal D}(\phi_0(q))}.
\]

So the strict-excess obstruction became:

\[
\boxed{
B_1>B_0+B_2
\iff
\Delta(q)\text{ has an interior critical point on the overlap interval.}
}
\]

This is, I think, the cleanest one-variable reduction of the strict-excess case. It parallels the updated paper’s nonmixed/global endgame, where the remaining burden is also a zero problem for one-variable gap functions \(G_{\xi,J}\). Here, on the fixed-shear side, the remaining burden is a critical-point problem for the one-variable inverse-branch gap \(\Delta\).

That unification is one of the nicest structural findings from the attack.

---

## 7. The transport-curvature observable \(\Xi\) was identified as the key integrability quantity

Differentiating the reciprocal-slope profiles further yields the natural observable
\[
\Xi(u):=\frac{\widehat{\mathcal D}'(u)}{\widehat{\mathcal D}(u)^3}
=
\frac{\widehat Q''(u)}{(\widehat Q'(u))^3}.
\]
On each outer run,
\[
R_j'(q)=-\Xi(\phi_j(q)).
\]
Equivalently, for the inverse branches,
\[
\phi_j''(q)=-\Xi(\phi_j(q)).
\]

This leads to a very sharp fork.

If \(\Xi\) is single-valued over \(q=\widehat Q(u)\) across the two outer runs — equivalently, if the two outer inverse branches have the same second derivative at equal \(q\)-value —
\[
\phi_0''(q)=\phi_2''(q),
\]
then the inverse-branch gap satisfies
\[
\Delta''(q)=0.
\]
So \(\Delta(q)\) is affine in \(q\). But strict excess forces an interior critical point of \(\Delta\), hence the affine function must actually be constant:
\[
\Delta(q)\equiv C.
\]

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{If }\Xi\text{ is single-valued over }\widehat Q,\text{ then strict excess forces constant-gap same-value transport.}
}
\]

That is a much cleaner integrability mechanism than the original amplitude inequality.

This led to the following canonical fork for the live fixed-shear obstruction:

- either \(\Xi\) descends to value space, in which case strict excess forces constant-gap transport;
- or \(\Xi\) does not descend to value space, and that failure is the first genuine nonlocal fixed-shear transport obstruction.

This is one of the strongest structural reductions of the entire attack.

---

## 8. Constant-gap transport was strengthened to affine same-value transport and local periodicity

From \(\Delta(q)\equiv C\), one gets
\[
\phi_2(q)=\phi_0(q)+C,
\]
hence the same-value transport map is affine:
\[
T(u)=u+C
\]
on the overlap interval.

Equivalently,
\[
\widehat Q(u+C)=\widehat Q(u)
\]
on an open interval of one outer run, with the shifted interval lying in the other outer run.

By analyticity, that local coincidence propagates on the whole connected overlap component. Therefore
\[
\widehat Q(u+C)=\widehat Q(u),\qquad
\widehat{\mathcal D}(u+C)=\widehat{\mathcal D}(u),
\]
and indeed all higher derivatives agree there too.

So strict excess plus value-space integrability of \(\Xi\) was upgraded from a pointwise coincidence to genuine local periodicity / translation symmetry of the quotient-visible transport tower.

That was a big gain.

---

## 9. Local periodicity was then shown incompatible with the three-run compression

This was the last major positive step.

The quotient-visible fixed-shear model already proves that, on a no-reentry branch, there are at most three sign-runs of \(\widehat{\mathcal D}\).

But if
\[
\widehat Q(u+C)=\widehat Q(u)
\]
on an open interval of the outer run \(J_0\), with shift into the outer run \(J_2\), then analyticity and endpoint matching force the whole outer run structure to translate. In particular, the adjacent sign pattern next to \(J_0\) is reproduced next to \(J_2\). That means the middle-run sign pattern is copied again beyond \(J_2\), creating another sign-run.

So affine same-value transport is incompatible with the already-proved three-run compression.

This yields the clean contradiction candidate:

> **No affine outer-run transport theorem.** In the quotient-visible exact fixed-shear three-run model, there is no nontrivial affine same-value transport
> \[
> \widehat Q(u+C)=\widehat Q(u)
> \]
> between the two outer runs.

Combining this with the \(\Xi\)-integrability reduction gives:

\[
\boxed{
\Xi=F(\widehat Q)\text{ across outer runs } \Longrightarrow B_1>B_0+B_2\text{ is impossible.}
}
\]

Together with sterility of equality, this would close the three-run quotient-visible fixed-shear lane completely.

This is probably the strongest positive result of the later stages of the attack, albeit still conditional on the \(\Xi\)-integrability step.

---

## 10. So the live fixed-shear endgame is now an exact fork

The fixed-shear lane is now reduced to a very precise fork.

### Route A: value-space integrability holds
There exists \(F\) such that
\[
\Xi(u)=\frac{\widehat Q''(u)}{(\widehat Q'(u))^3}=F(\widehat Q(u))
\]
across separated outer runs.

Then strict excess forces affine same-value transport, which forces local periodicity and hence forbidden run-pattern replication. So strict excess is impossible.

### Route B: value-space integrability fails
Then the first genuine remaining fixed-shear obstruction is exactly:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Failure of }\Xi(u)=\frac{\widehat Q''(u)}{(\widehat Q'(u))^3}\text{ to descend to a single-valued function of }\widehat Q\text{ across separated outer runs.}
}
\]

That is no longer vague. It is an exact nonlocal transport obstruction.

This is the sharpest current formulation of the remaining fixed-shear burden.

---

## 11. Structural findings

Here are the strongest structural findings that came out of the attack.

First, the mixed fixed-shear lane is now genuinely downstairs in quotient transport. The right objects are \(\widehat Q\), \(\widehat{\mathcal D}\), sign-run amplitudes \(B_j\), inverse branches \(\phi_j\), and the inverse-branch gap \(\Delta(q)\), not another local mixed branch taxonomy. That is fully consistent with the updated paper. 

Second, equality in the three-lobe criterion is sterile. It gives only boundary touching of value intervals, hence a zero-dimensional same-value set downstairs, and therefore cannot support a genuine local repeated-pair branch upstairs.

Third, strict excess has been repeatedly compressed:
\[
B_1>B_0+B_2
\]
is equivalent to open same-value transport, which forces an interior critical point of the inverse-branch gap \(\Delta(q)\), which under value-space integrability of \(\Xi\) forces \(\Delta\) to be constant, i.e. affine same-value transport.

Fourth, the entire live quotient-visible fixed-shear lane now looks like the same kind of one-variable endgame as the nonmixed/global lane. There, the remaining burden is zeros of endpoint-gap functions \(G_{\xi,J}\); here, it is interior critical points of the inverse-branch gap \(\Delta(q)\). That convergence is conceptually very satisfying and probably important strategically.

Fifth, the generator audit matters in a precise way: since no second primitive pointwise highest-new generator has appeared, the remaining fixed-shear obstruction should indeed be sought as a nonlocal transport statement, not as another pointwise field. The \(\Xi\)-integrability fork fits that perfectly. 

---

## 12. Negative findings

Here are the strongest negative findings.

First, I did **not** prove unconditionally that
\[
\Xi(u)=\frac{\widehat Q''(u)}{(\widehat Q'(u))^3}
\]
is single-valued over \(q=\widehat Q(u)\) across separated outer runs. That is still open.

Second, I did **not** identify a new pointwise generator or a new local algebraic obstruction. The updated paper’s negative audit remained intact and in fact guided the attack: the remaining problem is transport, not local field generation. 

Third, some earlier emphasis I placed on local cancellation-locus jet classification and rank-\(1\) first jets is now clearly secondary. Those ideas still say useful things about the local good-patch regime, but the fixed-shear endgame is not primarily a local cancellation-jet problem anymore. It is a quotient-transport gap problem. So that line should be demoted to auxiliary status.

Fourth, the strict-excess case has not been closed unconditionally. It has only been reduced to the transport-integrability fork described above.

---

## 13. Goodies

There were also several “goodies” that may be useful for draft or endgame shaping.

One is the clean inverse-branch formulation:
\[
\Delta(q)=\phi_2(q)-\phi_0(q).
\]
Then strict excess is exactly the existence of an interior critical point of \(\Delta\), and the value-space integrability condition is exactly
\[
\Delta''(q)=0.
\]
This is probably the cleanest mathematical normal form for the live fixed-shear obstruction.

Another is the equivalent formulation in terms of reciprocal-slope profiles:
\[
R_j(q)=\frac{1}{\widehat{\mathcal D}(\phi_j(q))}.
\]
Then strict excess forces an interior zero of \(R_2-R_0\), and value-space integrability means the two reciprocal-slope profiles satisfy the same scalar ODE. This may be the most intuitive transport interpretation.

A third is the observation that under \(\Xi\)-integrability, strict excess does not merely produce one point of jet coincidence; it produces an open family of same-value jet coincidences, i.e. local periodicity. That is much stronger than the original amplitude statement and makes the contradiction with three-run compression much more believable.

A fourth is the strong alignment with the paper’s global structure: both live remaining lanes are now gap-function problems. That should help the overall exposition.

---

## 14. Best current theorem targets

The sharpest remaining theorem targets now look like this.

### Fixed-shear target A: value-space integrability
Show that on separated outer runs of the actual RH quotient-visible fixed-shear branch,
\[
\Xi(u)=\frac{\widehat Q''(u)}{(\widehat Q'(u))^3}
\]
is single-valued over \(q=\widehat Q(u)\), equivalently
\[
\phi_0''(q)=\phi_2''(q)
\]
on the overlap interval.

### Fixed-shear target B: no affine outer-run transport
Show there is no nonzero \(C\) and open interval \(U\) with
\[
\widehat Q(u+C)=\widehat Q(u)
\qquad (u\in U),
\]
with \(U\) in one outer run and \(U+C\) in the other.

Together these would kill strict excess.

### Fixed-shear fallback target
If target A fails, characterize that failure explicitly as the first genuine nonlocal fixed-shear transport obstruction.

That would still be mathematically valuable, because it would identify the exact remaining burden rather than leaving it diffuse.

---

## 15. Current status in one paragraph

My current view is:

the fixed-shear quotient-visible lane has been reduced as far as possible by pure structural analysis. Equality is sterile. Strict excess is equivalent to an interior critical point of the inverse-branch gap \(\Delta(q)\). Under the natural value-space integrability condition for
\[
\Xi(u)=\frac{\widehat Q''(u)}{(\widehat Q'(u))^3},
\]
that critical-point condition forces \(\Delta\) to be constant, i.e. affine same-value transport, which by analyticity propagates to forbidden local periodicity and replication of the sign-run pattern, contradicting the already-proved three-run compression. So the live fixed-shear burden is now exactly the integrability fork for \(\Xi\): either prove \(\Xi\) descends to value space and the strict case dies, or recognize failure of that descent as the first genuine nonlocal fixed-shear obstruction.

That is the full state of the attack as I understand it.

## Assistant (2026-04-21 22:31:01)

I’m pushing directly on the remaining fork now. The goal is to see whether failure of value-space integrability for \(\Xi\) can itself be turned into a concrete new quotient transport observable, rather than just being named as an obstruction.

_Thought for 47s_

I think the next real step is to isolate the **exact defect observable** for the remaining fixed-shear lane.

Up to now the fork was:

- if
  \[
  \Xi(u):=\frac{\widehat Q''(u)}{(\widehat Q'(u))^3}
  \]
  is single-valued over \(q=\widehat Q(u)\) across the two outer runs, then strict excess forces affine same-value transport, hence forbidden run-pattern replication;
- if not, that failure is the first genuine nonlocal fixed-shear obstruction.

The new point is that this failure can be written as a single explicit scalar function on the overlap interval. That gives a much sharper target than just saying “integrability fails.”

---

## 1. The exact defect observable

Let \(\phi_0,\phi_2\) be the inverse branches of \(\widehat Q\) on the two outer runs over their common value interval \(\mathcal I\), and define the inverse-branch gap
\[
\Delta(q):=\phi_2(q)-\phi_0(q).
\]
Then
\[
\Delta'(q)
=
\frac{1}{\widehat{\mathcal D}(\phi_2(q))}
-
\frac{1}{\widehat{\mathcal D}(\phi_0(q))},
\]
and
\[
\Delta''(q)
=
-\Xi(\phi_2(q))+\Xi(\phi_0(q)).
\]

So the natural defect is
\[
\boxed{
\Lambda(q):=\Xi(\phi_2(q))-\Xi(\phi_0(q))=-\Delta''(q).
}
\]

This is the first explicit **nonlocal transport defect** for the strict three-run fixed-shear lane.

It measures exactly the failure of \(\Xi\) to descend to a single-valued function of the quotient value \(q=\widehat Q(u)\) across the two outer runs.

That is already a genuine advance: the obstruction is no longer vague. It is the scalar value-space defect \(\Lambda(q)\).

---

## 2. Why \(\Lambda\) is the right object

This cleans up the entire strict-excess story.

Strict excess
\[
B_1>B_0+B_2
\]
is equivalent to saying that \(\Delta\) has an interior critical point:
\[
\exists q_*\in \mathcal I\quad \Delta'(q_*)=0.
\]

Now:

- if \(\Lambda\equiv 0\), then \(\Delta''\equiv 0\), so \(\Delta\) is affine;
- since strict excess also forces an interior critical point of \(\Delta\), that affine function must in fact be constant;
- hence the same-value transport is affine:
  \[
  \phi_2(q)=\phi_0(q)+C,
  \]
  which is exactly the local periodicity / run-replication mechanism we already pushed into contradiction with the three-run compression. 

So:
\[
\boxed{
\Lambda\equiv 0 \Longrightarrow \text{strict excess collapses to forbidden affine outer-run transport.}
}
\]

Therefore any **surviving** strict-excess case must satisfy
\[
\Lambda\not\equiv 0.
\]

That is the sharpest possible statement of what remains.

---

## 3. The remaining lane is now a curvature-mismatch problem

Because
\[
\phi_j''(q)=-\Xi(\phi_j(q)),
\]
the defect \(\Lambda\) is exactly the mismatch of the second derivatives of the two outer inverse branches at equal value \(q\):
\[
\Lambda(q)=-(\phi_2''(q)-\phi_0''(q)).
\]

So the live fixed-shear obstruction is now:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Can the two outer inverse branches have an interior critical point of their gap } \Delta
\text{ while maintaining nontrivial inverse-curvature mismatch } \Lambda?
}
\]

That is a much more geometric formulation than the original amplitude inequality.

The equality case is already dead.
The \(\Lambda\equiv 0\) case is also dead.
So the only remaining possibility is now:

- \(\Delta'(q_*)=0\) for some interior \(q_*\),
- but \(\Lambda\) is not identically zero.

In other words, the entire live strict-excess lane has been compressed to a **nonzero curvature-mismatch at equal value** problem.

---

## 4. What happens at the interior critical point

Let \(q_*\in\mathcal I\) satisfy
\[
\Delta'(q_*)=0.
\]
Then
\[
\widehat Q(\phi_0(q_*))=\widehat Q(\phi_2(q_*))=q_*,
\qquad
\widehat{\mathcal D}(\phi_0(q_*))=\widehat{\mathcal D}(\phi_2(q_*)).
\]
So strict excess always produces a same-value / same-slope pair \((u_0,u_2)\) on the two outer runs.

At that same point,
\[
\Lambda(q_*)=\Xi(u_2)-\Xi(u_0).
\]

So the fork becomes extremely sharp:

- if \(\Lambda(q_*)=0\) and in fact \(\Lambda\equiv 0\), we are in the affine-transport contradiction;
- if \(\Lambda(q_*)\neq 0\), then the live strict-excess obstruction is exactly a same-value / same-slope pair with **different** transport-curvature observable \(\Xi\).

So the first genuine remaining fixed-shear obstruction is not just “\(\Xi\) is multivalued.” It is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{a separated pair with equal }(\widehat Q,\widehat{\mathcal D})\text{ but unequal }\Xi.
}
\]

That is the cleanest local-global obstruction I can see.

---

## 5. This yields a natural 3-jet map

This suggests the right transport map is not just
\[
u\mapsto (\widehat Q(u),\widehat{\mathcal D}(u))
\]
or
\[
u\mapsto \left(\widehat Q(u),\frac1{\widehat{\mathcal D}(u)}\right),
\]
but the 3-component map
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal J_3(u):=\left(\widehat Q(u),\widehat{\mathcal D}(u),\Xi(u)\right).
}
\]

Then the strict-excess lane has been reduced to:

- first, a self-intersection of the 2-jet projection
  \[
  (\widehat Q,\widehat{\mathcal D});
  \]
- second, either that self-intersection lifts to a self-intersection of \(\mathcal J_3\) as well (which forces affine transport and contradiction), or it does not (which means \(\Xi\) separates the pair and is therefore the first genuine nonlocal obstruction).

So the fixed-shear lane is now exactly a question of **3-jet separation** along the quotient-visible transport branch.

That is very much in the spirit of the updated generator audit: no new primitive pointwise generator, but possibly a nonlocal separation phenomenon at the level of transport jets. 

---

## 6. Best next theorem targets

This gives two extremely sharp theorem targets.

### Target A: vanishing of the defect observable
Show that on the actual RH quotient-visible fixed-shear branch,
\[
\Lambda(q)\equiv 0
\]
on any outer-run overlap interval.

Then strict excess collapses to affine transport and is impossible by the no-periodicity / no-run-replication argument.

### Target B: sign/variation control of the defect observable
Short of proving \(\Lambda\equiv 0\), show that \(\Lambda\) has a sign or variation law incompatible with an interior critical point of \(\Delta\).

For example, if \(\Lambda\) had one sign and suitable endpoint behavior, one might be able to show that \(\Delta\) cannot have the critical-point profile strict excess requires, or that any such critical point would propagate to forbidden recurrence.

This is probably the right fallback if exact value-space integrability is too strong.

---

## 7. Strongest new structural findings

I think the strongest structural findings from this round are these.

First, the live fixed-shear obstruction has now been compressed to a single explicit scalar defect
\[
\Lambda(q)=\Xi(\phi_2(q))-\Xi(\phi_0(q))=-\Delta''(q).
\]

Second, the entire strict-excess lane can now be restated as:
\[
\text{interior critical point of }\Delta \text{ + nontrivial curvature mismatch } \Lambda.
\]

Third, if \(\Lambda\equiv 0\), the strict-excess case is already dead by the affine-transport contradiction. So the only genuinely remaining fixed-shear possibility is
\[
\Lambda\not\equiv 0.
\]

Fourth, the first real unresolved object is no longer an amplitude \(B_j\), nor a new pointwise field. It is this nonlocal value-space curvature mismatch observable \(\Lambda\).

That is a very clean endpoint for the attack.

---

## 8. Negative findings

What I still do **not** have is an unconditional proof that

- \(\Lambda\equiv 0\), or
- \(\Lambda\) has a definite sign/variation law strong enough to exclude strict excess.

So the fixed-shear lane is not closed unconditionally.

But the important negative result is that there is now almost no ambiguity left about what remains. The live obstruction is no longer diffuse. It is exactly the behavior of \(\Lambda\) on the outer-run overlap interval.

---

## 9. Bottom line

The sharpest current summary of the fixed-shear attack is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The strict three-run fixed-shear obstruction has been reduced to the nonlocal value-space curvature defect }
\Lambda(q)=\Xi(\phi_2(q))-\Xi(\phi_0(q)).
}
\]

More explicitly:

- equality \(B_1=B_0+B_2\) is sterile;
- strict excess \(B_1>B_0+B_2\) is equivalent to an interior critical point of the inverse-branch gap \(\Delta\);
- if \(\Lambda\equiv 0\), then \(\Delta\) is affine, so strict excess forces forbidden local periodicity / run-pattern replication and dies;
- therefore any surviving fixed-shear obstruction must come from a **nontrivial curvature mismatch** \(\Lambda\), i.e. from equal \((\widehat Q,\widehat{\mathcal D})\) but unequal \(\Xi\) across separated outer runs.

That is the strongest reduction I can see right now.

## Assistant (2026-04-21 22:45:16)

I’m focusing only on the strict-excess fixed-shear fork now, using the consolidated picture as the baseline. The right object is the inverse-branch gap \(\Delta(q)=\phi_2(q)-\phi_0(q)\), so the next attack is to understand what an interior critical point of \(\Delta\) would force at the endpoints of the common value interval.

_Thought for 8s_

Here is the next push.

I think the best move now is to attack the strict-excess fixed-shear fork by exploiting the **endpoint singular behavior** of the inverse branches. That gives a sharper shape theorem for the inverse-branch gap
\[
\Delta(q)=\phi_2(q)-\phi_0(q)
\]
than I had before.

The key point is that strict excess is not just “\(\Delta\) has an interior critical point.” It is a much more rigid boundary-value problem: \(\Delta\) lives on a common value interval \(\mathcal I\) whose endpoints correspond to critical endpoints of the two outer runs, so \(\Delta'\) blows up with opposite signs at the two ends. That means any surviving obstruction must pass through a very specific one-dimensional geometry.

---

## 1. Endpoint asymptotics of the inverse branches

Let \(J_0,J_2\) be the two outer sign-runs of
\[
\widehat{\mathcal D}=\widehat Q'
\]
in the three-run quotient-visible fixed-shear model, and let
\[
\phi_0,\phi_2:\mathcal I\to J_0,J_2
\]
be the inverse branches on their common value interval \(\mathcal I\). Then
\[
\Delta(q):=\phi_2(q)-\phi_0(q),
\qquad
\Delta'(q)=\frac{1}{\widehat{\mathcal D}(\phi_2(q))}-\frac{1}{\widehat{\mathcal D}(\phi_0(q))}.
\]

At an endpoint \(q_-\) of \(\mathcal I\), exactly one of the two inverse branches approaches a critical endpoint of its run, so its slope reciprocal blows up, while the other branch stays away from criticality and contributes a finite term. At the other endpoint \(q_+\), the roles reverse.

So one has the asymptotic sign pattern
\[
\Delta'(q)\to -\infty \quad (q\downarrow q_-),
\qquad
\Delta'(q)\to +\infty \quad (q\uparrow q_+)
\]
after orienting the runs in the natural up–down–up picture. The exact sign convention is not important; what matters is that the endpoint signs are opposite.

This is stronger than just “there is an interior critical point.” It says:

\[
\boxed{
\text{In the strict-excess case, }\Delta\text{ must have at least one interior minimum.}
}
\]

Not just a critical point — an actual interior minimum.

---

## 2. Why this sharpens the live obstruction

So the remaining strict-excess fixed-shear obstruction is no longer arbitrary. It is:

- a \(C^\omega\) function \(\Delta\) on a bounded interval \(\mathcal I\),
- with opposite infinite-slope behavior at the endpoints,
- and with at least one interior minimum.

Now the curvature defect is
\[
\Lambda(q):=\Xi(\phi_2(q))-\Xi(\phi_0(q))=-\Delta''(q),
\]
where
\[
\Xi(u)=\frac{\widehat Q''(u)}{(\widehat Q'(u))^3}.
\]

So at any interior minimum \(q_*\) of \(\Delta\),
\[
\Delta'(q_*)=0,
\qquad
\Delta''(q_*)\ge 0,
\]
hence
\[
\Lambda(q_*)\le 0.
\]

This is the first pointwise sign information on the defect observable:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Any strict-excess obstruction forces a point }q_*\in \mathcal I
\text{ with }
\widehat Q(\phi_0(q_*))=\widehat Q(\phi_2(q_*)),
\ \widehat{\mathcal D}(\phi_0(q_*))=\widehat{\mathcal D}(\phi_2(q_*)),
\ \Xi(\phi_2(q_*))-\Xi(\phi_0(q_*))\le 0.
}
\]

So the first genuine nonlocal fixed-shear obstruction is not merely “equal \((\widehat Q,\widehat{\mathcal D})\) but unequal \(\Xi\).” It is more specific:

> equal \((\widehat Q,\widehat{\mathcal D})\), with the outer-run \(\Xi\)-difference having the sign needed to support an interior minimum of \(\Delta\).

That is already sharper.

---

## 3. If \(\Lambda\) has one sign, the strict case dies

This gives an immediate theorem schema.

Suppose one can prove on the actual RH quotient-visible fixed-shear branch that on any outer-run overlap interval,
\[
\Lambda(q)=\Xi(\phi_2(q))-\Xi(\phi_0(q))
\]
has strict positive sign:
\[
\Lambda(q)>0
\qquad (q\in\mathcal I).
\]
Then
\[
\Delta''(q)=-\Lambda(q)<0
\]
throughout \(\mathcal I\), so \(\Delta\) is strictly concave.

But a strictly concave function cannot have the endpoint derivative behavior
\[
\Delta'(q)\to -\infty \text{ at one end},\qquad \Delta'(q)\to +\infty \text{ at the other end},
\]
because for a concave function the derivative is monotone decreasing. So strict excess would be impossible.

Similarly, if \(\Lambda(q)<0\) everywhere, then \(\Delta\) is strictly convex, and in that case the endpoint derivative behavior is actually compatible with a unique interior minimum. So the sign matters very specifically.

Therefore the fixed-shear strict-excess lane can be killed by a one-sided inequality of exactly the right sign:

\[
\boxed{
\Lambda(q)>0 \text{ on every outer-run overlap interval } \Longrightarrow \text{strict excess impossible.}
}
\]

This is a much more targeted theorem than proving \(\Lambda\equiv 0\).

---

## 4. Comparison with the earlier integrability route

Earlier I reduced the problem to the integrable case \(\Lambda\equiv 0\), which implies \(\Delta''=0\), hence affine \(\Delta\), hence forbidden affine same-value transport and run-pattern replication.

That route is still valid and strong.

But the new observation is that one does not need full vanishing of \(\Lambda\). A sign theorem of the right orientation could already suffice.

So the fixed-shear endgame now has two plausible closure routes:

### Route A: full value-space integrability
\[
\Lambda\equiv 0.
\]
Then \(\Delta\) is affine, and strict excess forces forbidden affine transport.

### Route B: curvature-sign separation
\[
\Lambda(q)>0
\]
on overlap intervals.
Then \(\Delta\) is strictly concave, incompatible with the endpoint derivative blow-up pattern required by strict excess.

This is a useful improvement, because Route B is weaker than full integrability and may be easier to prove from the RH transport law.

---

## 5. The endpoint blow-up also gives uniqueness if \(\Lambda<0\)

There is another structural goodie here.

If instead one had
\[
\Lambda(q)<0
\]
on the overlap interval, then
\[
\Delta''(q)>0,
\]
so \(\Delta\) is strictly convex. Combined with the endpoint derivative blow-up pattern, this would force exactly one interior minimum. Therefore:

- the strict-excess branch would not be arbitrary;
- it would be organized by a unique same-value / same-slope pair downstairs.

So even the “wrong-sign” case gives a strong normal form.

That means the sign of \(\Lambda\) completely controls the fixed-shear strict-excess geometry:

- \(\Lambda>0\): impossible;
- \(\Lambda\equiv 0\): affine transport, hence impossible by run replication;
- \(\Lambda<0\): unique minimum regime.

So the whole lane has now been reduced to a sign law for a single scalar defect.

That is the cleanest reduction so far.

---

## 6. A canonical theorem target

The best theorem target I see now is:

### Outer-run curvature-separation theorem
On the actual RH quotient-visible exact fixed-shear branch, whenever two separated outer runs admit a common value interval \(\mathcal I\), one has
\[
\Xi(\phi_2(q))-\Xi(\phi_0(q))>0
\qquad (q\in\mathcal I),
\]
where
\[
\Xi(u)=\frac{\widehat Q''(u)}{(\widehat Q'(u))^3}.
\]

Then strict excess is impossible.

A weaker but still useful version would be:

### No wrong-curvature minimum theorem
At any same-value / same-slope pair between separated outer runs, the sign of the curvature mismatch \(\Xi(\phi_2)-\Xi(\phi_0)\) is incompatible with being an interior minimum of \(\Delta\).

That would kill the strict-excess obstruction directly at the critical point.

---

## 7. Why this fits the consolidated picture

This is well aligned with the consolidated paper update.

The fixed-shear lane is no longer about finding a new local field. The generator audit says that ceiling has already been reached. The remaining issue is nonlocal quotient transport. The scalar defect
\[
\Lambda(q)=\Xi(\phi_2(q))-\Xi(\phi_0(q))
\]
is exactly such a nonlocal transport quantity: it compares the same explicit pointwise observable \(\Xi\) at two separated points connected only through equal value downstairs. That is exactly the kind of object one should expect to survive after the pointwise audit. 

And just as on the nonmixed/global side the remaining burden is zeros of monotone endpoint-gap functions, here the remaining burden has now become sign/critical-point control for the inverse-branch gap \(\Delta\) through the sign of \(\Lambda\). So both residual lanes are now genuinely one-variable transport-gap problems.

---

## 8. Strongest new structural findings

The strongest new findings from this round are:

First, strict excess forces not merely a critical point of \(\Delta\), but an interior **minimum**, thanks to the opposite infinite-slope behavior of \(\Delta'\) at the ends of the overlap interval.

Second, the defect observable
\[
\Lambda(q)=\Xi(\phi_2(q))-\Xi(\phi_0(q))=-\Delta''(q)
\]
has a direct geometric meaning: it is the curvature mismatch of the two outer inverse branches in value space.

Third, the sign of \(\Lambda\) completely controls the strict-excess geometry:
- \(\Lambda>0\) kills it;
- \(\Lambda\equiv 0\) yields affine transport and then contradiction;
- \(\Lambda<0\) forces a unique minimum regime.

So the live fixed-shear lane is now a sign law for a single value-space curvature defect.

---

## 9. Honest status

I do **not** yet know the sign of \(\Lambda\) on the actual RH branch.

So this is not closure.

But it is a real reduction: the remaining fixed-shear burden is no longer “some nonlocal transport issue.” It is now exactly:

\[
\boxed{
\text{determine the sign or variation law of }
\Lambda(q)=\Xi(\phi_2(q))-\Xi(\phi_0(q))
\text{ on outer-run overlap intervals.}
}
\]

That is the sharpest current continuation I can see.
