## Assistant (2026-04-22 02:12:32)

_Thought for 13s_

Here is the next attack.

The strongest move now is to keep the corrected overlap regime
\[
B_0+B_2>B_1
\]
and push the witness chord analysis into a genuine **moment problem** for \(\widehat Q'''\). That is sharper than the previous \(K_2\)-sign discussion and gives a concrete obstruction shape.

We have a witness \(q_*\in\mathcal I\) with outer points
\[
u_0:=\phi_0(q_*),\qquad u_2:=\phi_2(q_*),\qquad d:=u_2-u_0>0,
\]
satisfying
\[
\widehat Q(u_0)=\widehat Q(u_2)=q_*,
\qquad
\widehat Q'(u_0)=\widehat Q'(u_2)=:p\neq 0.
\]
As before, define
\[
R(u):=\widehat Q(u)-q_*-p(u-u_0).
\]
Then
\[
R(u_0)=R'(u_0)=R(u_2)=R'(u_2)=0,
\]
so \(R\) has exact quartic Hermite factorization
\[
R(u)=(u-u_0)^2(u-u_2)^2S(u).
\]

The first useful exact identity is the one from the previous step:
\[
K_2(q_*)=\frac{\widehat Q''(u_0)-\widehat Q''(u_2)}{p^3}
=-\frac1{p^3}\int_{u_0}^{u_2}\widehat Q'''(u)\,du.
\]
So \(K_2<0\) is exactly positive total \(\widehat Q'''\)-mass on the witness chord.

Now I want to refine that using the **endpoint constraints** more strongly.

Because \(\widehat Q'(u_0)=\widehat Q'(u_2)\), we also have
\[
\int_{u_0}^{u_2}\widehat Q''(u)\,du=0.
\]
And because \(\widehat Q(u_0)=\widehat Q(u_2)-p(u_2-u_0)\), we get
\[
\int_{u_0}^{u_2}(u-u_0)\widehat Q''(u)\,du=0.
\]
Indeed, integrating by parts:
\[
\int_{u_0}^{u_2}(u-u_0)\widehat Q''(u)\,du
=
(u-u_0)\widehat Q'(u)\Big|_{u_0}^{u_2}
-\int_{u_0}^{u_2}\widehat Q'(u)\,du
=
dp-(\widehat Q(u_2)-\widehat Q(u_0))=0.
\]

That is a real gain: the witness chord is not just a same-value / same-slope chord. It also makes \(\widehat Q''\) orthogonal to both \(1\) and \(u-u_0\) on the chord.

Now integrate by parts once more, but with \(\widehat Q'''\). Set \(x=u-u_0\in[0,d]\). Then
\[
\int_0^d \widehat Q'''(u_0+x)\,dx
=
\widehat Q''(u_2)-\widehat Q''(u_0),
\]
which is the \(K_2\)-identity above.

But also
\[
\int_0^d x\,\widehat Q'''(u_0+x)\,dx
=
d\,\widehat Q''(u_2)-\int_0^d \widehat Q''(u_0+x)\,dx
=
d\,\widehat Q''(u_2),
\]
because the zeroth moment of \(\widehat Q''\) on the chord is zero. Similarly,
\[
\int_0^d (d-x)\,\widehat Q'''(u_0+x)\,dx
=
-d\,\widehat Q''(u_0).
\]

So the endpoint second derivatives are exactly the first moments of \(\widehat Q'''\):
\[
\boxed{
\widehat Q''(u_2)=\frac1d\int_{u_0}^{u_2}(u-u_0)\widehat Q'''(u)\,du,
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\widehat Q''(u_0)=-\frac1d\int_{u_0}^{u_2}(u_2-u)\widehat Q'''(u)\,du.
}
\]

Subtracting them reproduces the total-mass formula for \(K_2\), but now we see more:

a bad sign of \(K_2\) means not only that the total mass
\[
\int_{u_0}^{u_2}\widehat Q'''(u)\,du
\]
has the wrong sign. It means the **right-weighted first moment** dominates the left-weighted one:
\[
\int_{u_0}^{u_2}(u-u_0)\widehat Q'''(u)\,du
>
-\int_{u_0}^{u_2}(u_2-u)\widehat Q'''(u)\,du
\]
assuming \(p>0\).

That is a stronger obstruction shape.

Now combine that with the Rolle package forced by the quartic contact. Since \(R\) has double zeros at both endpoints, \(R''=\widehat Q''\) has at least two interior zeros, and \(R'''=\widehat Q'''\) has at least one interior zero. So on any witness chord:

- \(\widehat Q''\) changes sign at least twice;
- \(\widehat Q'''\) changes sign at least once.

Thus a negative \(K_2\)-dip would require a sign-changing \(\widehat Q'''\) whose **total mass** and **first moment** are both biased in the same direction strongly enough to produce endpoint asymmetry of \(\widehat Q''\).

That is much more rigid than the previous formulation.

There is an even cleaner centered version. Let
\[
m:=\frac{u_0+u_2}{2},\qquad y:=u-m,\qquad y\in[-d/2,d/2].
\]
Then
\[
\widehat Q''(u_2)-\widehat Q''(u_0)
=
\int_{-d/2}^{d/2}\widehat Q'''(m+y)\,dy,
\]
while the witness conditions imply
\[
\int_{-d/2}^{d/2}\widehat Q''(m+y)\,dy=0,
\qquad
\int_{-d/2}^{d/2} y\,\widehat Q''(m+y)\,dy=0.
\]
So the witness chord is centered in such a way that \(\widehat Q''\) has both zero mean and zero first moment on the chord. Any bad sign of \(K_2\) is therefore entirely coming from the **odd part** of \(\widehat Q'''\) around the chord midpoint.

That leads to the sharpest new theorem target I can see:

\[
\boxed{
\text{On every same-value / same-slope outer witness chord, the odd part of }\widehat Q''' \text{ about the chord midpoint has nonpositive total mass.}
}
\]

Because that is exactly what would force
\[
\int_{u_0}^{u_2}\widehat Q'''(u)\,du\le 0,
\]
hence
\[
K_2(q_*)\ge 0.
\]

And if \(K_2\ge 0\) at every witness, then since \(K_2>0\) near both ends of the overlap interval, \(K_1\) is monotone increasing and the whole overlap lane collapses to a unique witness.

So the overlap lane has now been reduced to this concrete moment question:

> Can a sign-changing \(\widehat Q'''\) on a witness chord, already constrained by the quartic endpoint contact and the two vanishing moments of \(\widehat Q''\), still have the wrong signed total mass?

That is a much sharper target than “analyze \(K_2\)” abstractly.

The strongest new structural finding is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{A bad overlap witness would force a chord on which }\widehat Q'' \text{ has zero mean and zero first moment, while }\widehat Q''' \text{ still has biased total mass.}
}
\]

That is a very rigid package.

So the next attack I would actually push is to prove a **moment-sign theorem** for \(\widehat Q'''\) on same-value / same-slope outer witness chords. If that lands, we get \(K_2\ge 0\), hence uniqueness of the overlap witness, and the live lane becomes far more manageable.

## Assistant (2026-04-22 02:16:00)

_Thought for 7s_

Here is the next push.

The strongest move now is to stop looking only at the **total mass**
\[
\int_{u_0}^{u_2}\widehat Q'''(u)\,du
\]
and use the quartic-contact witness to extract an exact **orthogonality package** for \(\widehat Q''\) and \(\widehat Q'''\) on the chord. That gives a much tighter necessary condition for any bad overlap witness.

We are in the corrected live regime
\[
B_0+B_2>B_1,
\]
with a same-value / same-slope witness chord
\[
u_0<u_2,\qquad \widehat Q(u_0)=\widehat Q(u_2),\qquad \widehat Q'(u_0)=\widehat Q'(u_2)=p\neq 0.
\]
As before, set
\[
R(u):=\widehat Q(u)-\widehat Q(u_0)-p(u-u_0).
\]
Then
\[
R(u_0)=R'(u_0)=R(u_2)=R'(u_2)=0,
\]
so
\[
R(u)=(u-u_0)^2(u-u_2)^2S(u).
\]

This already implies the Rolle package:
- at least two interior zeros of \(\widehat Q''=R''\),
- at least one interior zero of \(\widehat Q'''=R'''\).

But there is more.

Let
\[
m:=\frac{u_0+u_2}{2},\qquad y:=u-m,\qquad a:=\frac{u_2-u_0}{2}.
\]
Then the chord is \([m-a,m+a]\). In centered form,
\[
R(m+y)=\bigl(y^2-a^2\bigr)^2\,\widetilde S(y),
\]
for an analytic \(\widetilde S\).

Now integrate by parts carefully. Since
\[
\widehat Q(u_2)-\widehat Q(u_0)=p(u_2-u_0),
\]
we already know
\[
\int_{u_0}^{u_2}\widehat Q''(u)\,du=0.
\]
And since
\[
(u-u_0)\widehat Q'(u)\Big|_{u_0}^{u_2}=dp,\qquad \int_{u_0}^{u_2}\widehat Q'(u)\,du=dp,
\]
we also have
\[
\int_{u_0}^{u_2}(u-u_0)\widehat Q''(u)\,du=0.
\]
Centering this gives the cleaner pair
\[
\boxed{
\int_{-a}^{a}\widehat Q''(m+y)\,dy=0,
\qquad
\int_{-a}^{a} y\,\widehat Q''(m+y)\,dy=0.
}
\]

So at every same-value / same-slope outer witness, \(\widehat Q''\) has both **zero mean** and **zero first moment** on the chord.

That is already a strong constraint.

Now differentiate the second identity by parts:
\[
0=\int_{-a}^{a} y\,\widehat Q''(m+y)\,dy
=
\left[\frac{y^2}{2}\widehat Q''(m+y)\right]_{-a}^{a}
-\frac12\int_{-a}^{a} y^2\,\widehat Q'''(m+y)\,dy.
\]
So
\[
\boxed{
\int_{-a}^{a} y^2\,\widehat Q'''(m+y)\,dy
=
a^2\bigl(\widehat Q''(u_2)-\widehat Q''(u_0)\bigr).
}
\]

Since
\[
K_2(q_*)=\frac{\widehat Q''(u_0)-\widehat Q''(u_2)}{p^3},
\]
this becomes
\[
\boxed{
K_2(q_*)
=
-\frac{1}{a^2p^3}\int_{-a}^{a} y^2\,\widehat Q'''(m+y)\,dy.
}
\]

This is much sharper than the earlier total-mass formula. It says the next transport defect is not controlled by the plain mass of \(\widehat Q'''\), but by its **quadratic moment about the chord midpoint**.

So a bad sign \(K_2(q_*)<0\) forces
\[
\int_{-a}^{a} y^2\,\widehat Q'''(m+y)\,dy>0
\quad\text{(assuming }p>0\text{)}.
\]

That is a very rigid statement, because \(y^2\) kills the sign of the odd part and emphasizes the chord flanks. In other words:

> a bad overlap witness requires the third derivative to be positively biased on the chord flanks strongly enough to overcome the internal sign changes forced by the Rolle package.

That is a better obstruction shape than the raw total-mass statement.

There is a second useful identity. Since
\[
\widehat Q''(u_2)-\widehat Q''(u_0)=\int_{u_0}^{u_2}\widehat Q'''(u)\,du,
\]
we also have
\[
\int_{-a}^{a}\widehat Q'''(m+y)\,dy
=
\widehat Q''(u_2)-\widehat Q''(u_0).
\]
Comparing with the weighted formula above gives
\[
\boxed{
\int_{-a}^{a}(y^2-a^2)\,\widehat Q'''(m+y)\,dy=0.
}
\]

That is the cleanest moment identity so far.

So every same-value / same-slope outer witness satisfies:

\[
\boxed{
\int_{-a}^{a}\widehat Q''(m+y)\,dy=0,
\qquad
\int_{-a}^{a} y\,\widehat Q''(m+y)\,dy=0,
\qquad
\int_{-a}^{a}(y^2-a^2)\,\widehat Q'''(m+y)\,dy=0.
}
\]

These are exact.

Now combine them with the quartic-contact Rolle package:

- \(\widehat Q''\) has at least two interior zeros on the chord,
- \(\widehat Q'''\) has at least one interior zero on the chord,
- yet \(\widehat Q''\) has zero mean and zero first moment,
- and \(\widehat Q'''\) satisfies the weighted identity above.

This means a bad overlap witness is no longer just “same value, same slope, plus some sign change.” It is a chord carrying a very specific **moment-balanced oscillation pattern**.

That suggests the sharpest next theorem target I can see:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Prove a sign/moment theorem for }\widehat Q''' \text{ on a same-value / same-slope outer witness chord, sufficient to force }
\int_{-a}^{a} y^2\,\widehat Q'''(m+y)\,dy\le 0.
}
\]

If that holds, then \(K_2(q_*)\ge 0\) at every witness. Since \(K_2>0\) near both ends of the overlap interval, \(K_1\) is monotone increasing, so the overlap lane collapses to a unique witness.

This is, I think, the cleanest current attack because it isolates an exact integral quantity:

- not the full function \(H_2\),
- not the full regularized defect \(E\),
- but the midpoint quadratic moment of \(\widehat Q'''\).

That is the strongest sharpening I can currently make.

## Assistant (2026-04-22 02:19:00)

_Thought for 53s_

Here is the next real attack.

The strongest sharpening now is to recenter the quartic-contact factorization at the **midpoint of the witness chord**. Once you do that, the live overlap defect splits cleanly into an **even** and **odd** part, and the next transport defect \(K_2\) is seen to depend **only on the odd part**. That is a real structural gain, and it matches the draft’s current emphasis on same-value / same-slope witnesses plus higher-rung transport data on the genuine overlap lane \(B_0+B_2>B_1\).【180†source】【181†source】

Take a same-value / same-slope witness chord
\[
u_0<u_2,\qquad \widehat Q(u_0)=\widehat Q(u_2),\qquad \widehat Q'(u_0)=\widehat Q'(u_2)=p\neq 0.
\]
Set
\[
m:=\frac{u_0+u_2}{2},\qquad a:=\frac{u_2-u_0}{2},\qquad y:=u-m\in[-a,a].
\]
Then the quartic Hermite factorization becomes
\[
\widehat Q(m+y)=q_*+p(y+a)+\bigl(y^2-a^2\bigr)^2\,T(y),
\]
for an analytic coefficient \(T\) on the chord. Here \(T\) is just the centered version of the earlier witness coefficient \(S\).

Now decompose
\[
T=T_{\mathrm{even}}+T_{\mathrm{odd}}
\]
into midpoint-even and midpoint-odd parts.

This immediately gives the first strong formula. Since
\[
\widehat Q''(m\pm a)=8a^2\,T(\pm a),
\]
the next transport defect at the witness is
\[
K_2(q_*)=\frac{\widehat Q''(u_0)-\widehat Q''(u_2)}{p^3}
=
\frac{8a^2}{p^3}\bigl(T(-a)-T(a)\bigr)
=
-\frac{16a^2}{p^3}\,T_{\mathrm{odd}}(a).
\]

So:

\[
\boxed{
K_2(q_*) \text{ depends only on the midpoint-odd part of the quartic coefficient }T.
}
\]

That is the cleanest new structural finding.

In particular, assuming \(p>0\),

- \(K_2(q_*)=0\) iff \(T_{\mathrm{odd}}(a)=0\),
- \(K_2(q_*)<0\) iff \(T_{\mathrm{odd}}(a)>0\),
- \(K_2(q_*)>0\) iff \(T_{\mathrm{odd}}(a)<0\).

So a bad negative dip of \(K_2\) is **exactly** a positive midpoint-parity defect of the witness coefficient at the chord boundary.

That is much sharper than any earlier phrasing in terms of raw transport mass.

There is a second gain. If \(T\) is midpoint-even, then \(\bigl(y^2-a^2\bigr)^2T(y)\) is even, so its third derivative is odd. Hence \(\widehat Q'''(m+y)\) is odd on the chord, and all even weighted moments vanish automatically. In particular,
\[
\int_{-a}^{a} y^2\,\widehat Q'''(m+y)\,dy=0,
\]
so \(K_2(q_*)=0\). Thus the whole problematic overlap geometry is driven entirely by **midpoint-odd asymmetry** of \(T\).

Equivalently: the same-value / same-slope witness itself is not the dangerous thing. The dangerous thing is failure of **midpoint symmetry** of the quartic-contact remainder.

That suggests the cleanest next theorem target I can see:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Prove a midpoint-parity theorem for the witness coefficient }T,\text{ or at least show }T_{\mathrm{odd}}(a)\le 0.
}
\]

If that holds, then \(K_2(q_*)\ge 0\) at every witness. Since \(K_2>0\) near both ends of the overlap interval, \(K_1\) is monotone increasing, so the whole overlap lane collapses to a unique witness.

There is also a useful weaker version:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Show that the midpoint-odd part }T_{\mathrm{odd}}\text{ cannot have positive boundary sign on a witness chord.}
}
\]

That is weaker than full midpoint-evenness, but it is exactly what is needed to rule out \(K_2<0\).

This also clarifies the role of the earlier moment formulas. The identity
\[
K_2(q_*)=-\frac{1}{p^3}\int_{u_0}^{u_2}\widehat Q'''(u)\,du
\]
is still true, but now we see why: only the midpoint-even part of \(\widehat Q'''\) contributes to that integral, and that midpoint-even part comes exactly from the midpoint-odd part of \(T\). So the third-derivative mass picture was really a parity-defect picture in disguise.

That is the second strong structural gain.

So the sharpened attack is now this:

- stay only in the genuine overlap regime \(B_0+B_2>B_1\);
- isolate a same-value / same-slope witness \(K_1=0\);
- recenter the quartic-contact factorization at the chord midpoint;
- split the witness coefficient into even/odd parts;
- attack the sign of the odd part at the boundary, since that alone controls \(K_2\).

I do **not** have the theorem yet. But this is the sharpest reduction I can honestly claim:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The live overlap lane has been reduced to a midpoint-parity defect problem for the quartic witness coefficient }T.
}
\]

That is, I think, the strongest attack currently available.

_Thought for 2m 9s_

I found an important correction, and it sharpens the attack by showing exactly what **cannot** work.

The earlier quartic-contact factorization I was using was too naive: for a same-value / same-slope witness chord, the correct baseline is not affine. It is the **cubic Hermite interpolant** matching equal endpoint values and equal endpoint slopes.

That changes the local witness calculus in a decisive way.

---

## 1. Correct local factorization at a same-value / same-slope witness

Take a genuine overlap witness on the corrected live regime
\[
B_0+B_2>B_1,
\]
so there is a point \(q_*\in\mathcal I\) with outer points
\[
u_0<u_2,\qquad \widehat Q(u_0)=\widehat Q(u_2)=q_*,
\qquad \widehat Q'(u_0)=\widehat Q'(u_2)=p\neq 0.
\]

Center the chord:
\[
m:=\frac{u_0+u_2}{2},\qquad a:=\frac{u_2-u_0}{2},\qquad y:=u-m\in[-a,a].
\]

The unique cubic Hermite interpolant satisfying
\[
P(-a)=P(a)=q_*,\qquad P'(-a)=P'(a)=p
\]
is
\[
P(y)=q_*+p\left(\frac{y^3}{2a^2}-\frac y2\right).
\]

So the **correct** exact factorization is
\[
\boxed{
\widehat Q(m+y)
=
q_*+p\left(\frac{y^3}{2a^2}-\frac y2\right)
+
(y^2-a^2)^2\,T(y),
}
\]
for an analytic coefficient \(T\).

This is the right witness normal form.

That is the first important correction.

---

## 2. Exact formula for \(K_2\) in the corrected normal form

Now compute
\[
K_2(q_*)=\frac{\widehat Q''(u_0)-\widehat Q''(u_2)}{p^3}.
\]

Using the corrected factorization, one gets the exact endpoint formula
\[
\boxed{
\widehat Q''(u_0)-\widehat Q''(u_2)
=
-\frac{6p}{a}
+
8a^2\bigl(T(-a)-T(a)\bigr).
}
\]

So
\[
\boxed{
K_2(q_*)
=
-\frac{6}{a\,p^2}
+
\frac{8a^2}{p^3}\bigl(T(-a)-T(a)\bigr).
}
\]

This is the real local formula.

And it immediately changes the picture:

- there is a **universal negative baseline contribution**
  \[
  -\frac{6}{a\,p^2},
  \]
  coming from the cubic Hermite interpolant itself;
- the quartic coefficient \(T\) only contributes through the endpoint odd asymmetry
  \[
  T(-a)-T(a).
  \]

So the sign of \(K_2\) is not controlled purely by the quartic remainder. There is already a built-in cubic contribution of fixed sign.

That is a major sharpening.

---

## 3. Immediate no-go: purely local sign theorems for \(K_2\) are false

This corrected formula gives a very strong negative result.

If I take \(T\equiv 0\), then the witness is just the cubic Hermite interpolant, and
\[
K_2(q_*)=-\frac{6}{a\,p^2}<0
\qquad (\text{for }p\neq 0).
\]

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{A same-value / same-slope local witness can already have }K_2<0\text{ with no quartic correction at all.}
}
\]

That means any theorem of the form

- “every local witness has \(K_2\ge 0\),”
- or “the quartic witness coefficient alone forces \(K_2\ge 0\),”
- or “purely local quartic-contact geometry kills the overlap lane”

is simply false.

This is the strongest no-go I have found in this lane.

It means the overlap lane cannot be closed by **purely local witness geometry** at the level of same-value / same-slope contact. One needs genuinely global or branch-dependent input.

That is completely in line with the current draft’s ceiling statements: the remaining burden is transport/package-level, not “one more local sign lemma.”【180†source】【181†source】

---

## 4. What survives from the previous attack

The reciprocal-slope tower itself is still the right framework:

\[
J_1(u)=\frac1{\widehat Q'(u)},\qquad
J_{n+1}(u)=J_1(u)\partial_u J_n(u),
\qquad
K_n(q)=J_n(\phi_2(q))-J_n(\phi_0(q)),
\qquad
K_{n+1}=K_n'.
\]

And in the corrected overlap regime \(B_0+B_2>B_1\), one still has:

- \(K_1\) has opposite endpoint signs, so there is at least one witness \(K_1=0\);
- \(K_2\) is positive near both ends of the overlap interval;
- any interior negative dip of \(K_2\) forces a higher-rung witness \(K_3=0\) with \(K_2<0\).

All of that still holds.

What changes is this:

> the sign of \(K_2\) at a local witness is **not** determined by local quartic remainder geometry alone.

There is a built-in cubic Hermite bias.

So the true remaining question is not local sign of \(T\), but whether the **global branch transport** can ever realize the endpoint asymmetry
\[
8a^2\bigl(T(-a)-T(a)\bigr)
\]
large enough to overcome the universal negative baseline
\[
\frac{6p}{a}.
\]

That is a much sharper and more honest formulation.

---

## 5. Sharpened interpretation of a bad overlap witness

From the exact formula
\[
K_2(q_*)
=
-\frac{6}{a\,p^2}
+
\frac{8a^2}{p^3}\bigl(T(-a)-T(a)\bigr),
\]
a negative \(K_2\)-dip means either:

- the quartic asymmetry is too small to overcome the cubic baseline; or
- in the strongest bad case, it is positive but still not large enough.

A positive \(K_2\) at a witness requires the endpoint asymmetry to satisfy
\[
T(-a)-T(a)>\frac{3p}{4a^3}.
\]

So the overlap lane has become a very concrete threshold problem:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Can the global outer-shell transport force quartic endpoint asymmetry above the threshold } \frac{3p}{4a^3}\text{?}
}
\]

That is much more precise than anything I had before.

---

## 6. Best new theorem target

The cleanest next theorem target is now:

### Threshold asymmetry theorem
At every same-value / same-slope outer witness chord,
\[
T(-a)-T(a)\le \frac{3p}{4a^3}.
\]

Then
\[
K_2(q_*)\le 0
\]
at every witness.

Combined with the fact that \(K_2>0\) near both ends of the overlap interval, this would force a very rigid witness structure and likely imply that any witness must occur only after \(K_2\) has already turned upward again, which is a much more constrained geometry than before.

A stronger version would be:

### Strict threshold gap theorem
\[
T(-a)-T(a)< \frac{3p}{4a^3}
\]
for every witness chord.

Then \(K_2<0\) at every witness, which when combined with endpoint positivity of \(K_2\) would force at least two zeros of \(K_2\) and therefore an interior \(K_3=0\) witness. That would push the whole lane one rung higher automatically.

So the overlap lane is now best attacked as a **threshold asymmetry problem** for the corrected quartic coefficient \(T\), not as a pure sign problem.

---

## 7. What this means strategically

This corrected computation says something important about where to spend effort.

It is probably **not** worth trying to prove a purely local theorem like “\(K_2\ge 0\) at every witness” or “\(T(-a)\ge T(a)\)” from the local witness factorization alone. Those are false as purely local statements.

The right next attacks are instead:

1. a **global transport closure law** on the outer shells, e.g.
   \[
   \widehat Q''=G(\widehat Q,\widehat Q'),
   \]
   which would constrain the allowed endpoint asymmetry of \(T\);

2. a **higher-rung separation theorem** in the reciprocal-slope tower \((\widehat Q,J_1,J_2,\dots)\), since local witness geometry alone is too flexible;

3. or a **scalar-local close-carrier theorem** from the other mixed lane, together with an independent proof that any surviving overlap witness must enter the close regime.

That is much more in line with the current draft’s division of labor.【181†source】

---

## 8. Strongest new structural finding

The strongest new result from this attack is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The overlap witness calculus has a universal cubic Hermite baseline, and }K_2\text{ is a thresholded endpoint-asymmetry invariant, not a pure quartic sign invariant.}
}
\]

This is a real correction and a real sharpening.

It means the local witness normal form by itself cannot close the overlap lane. Any successful closure must use something genuinely global/transport/package-level beyond that normal form.

---

## 9. Bottom line

So the best current attack is now:

- keep the corrected overlap regime \(B_0+B_2>B_1\);
- use the reciprocal-slope tower for the transport side;
- use the corrected Hermite factorization
  \[
  \widehat Q(m+y)=q_*+p\left(\frac{y^3}{2a^2}-\frac y2\right)+(y^2-a^2)^2T(y);
  \]
- and attack the **threshold asymmetry**
  \[
  T(-a)-T(a)-\frac{3p}{4a^3}.
  \]

That is the sharpest theorem-level quantity I can isolate right now. It is also the cleanest indication that the remaining overlap lane really is not a local problem anymore.

# 1. Corrected regime picture

One of the most important corrections was the sign flip in the three-run lobe trichotomy:

\[
B_0+B_2>B_1 \quad\text{open outer overlap,}
\]
\[
B_0+B_2=B_1 \quad\text{touching,}
\]
\[
B_1>B_0+B_2 \quad\text{separation.}
\]

So the whole \(\phi_0,\phi_2,\Delta,\Xi\) transport setup only belongs to the **overlap** case, not to the separation case. This is now a structural correction that should be kept explicit in every downstream argument. 【180†source】

That means a number of my earlier transport reductions were attached to the wrong inequality. The transport machinery itself survives; the regime assignment had to be corrected.

This is now part of the stable picture.

---

# 2. What remains genuinely live on the mixed side

Consistent with the consolidated notes, the only genuinely live mixed corner is the exact fixed-shear corner
\[
\{S=0\}\cap\{K_v=0\},
\]
and the correct live analysis there is quotient-visible and downstairs in \(u=t^2\). The mixed side splits as:

- \((K_v=0,S\neq 0)\): already mixed low-order;
- \((S=0,K_v\neq 0)\): transfers into nonmixed 4-point geometry;
- only the exact fixed-shear corner remains genuinely live. 【180†source】【181†source】

So the live lane is not another local “hidden reset” problem. It is a transport / package problem on the quotient branch. That broad structural point is already in the updated notes and I agree with it. 【180†source】【181†source】

---

# 3. Reciprocal-slope tower: the right transport hierarchy

Inside the corrected live overlap regime \(B_0+B_2>B_1\), let
\[
\phi_0,\phi_2:\mathcal I\to J_0,J_2
\]
be the inverse branches on the common value interval, so
\[
\widehat Q(\phi_0(q))=\widehat Q(\phi_2(q))=q.
\]

Then define
\[
J_1(u):=\frac1{\widehat Q'(u)},\qquad
J_{n+1}(u):=J_1(u)\partial_u J_n(u),
\]
and
\[
K_n(q):=J_n(\phi_2(q))-J_n(\phi_0(q)).
\]

A basic but very useful exact identity is:
\[
\boxed{
K_{n+1}(q)=\frac{d}{dq}K_n(q).
}
\]

This means the whole live overlap transport problem is a one-variable derivative tower.

That is one of the cleanest structural gains of the whole attack.

It aligns with the updated note’s recommendation to think in terms of the reciprocal-slope tower and higher-rung same-value / same-slope / even-jet witnesses. 【181†source】

---

# 4. Endpoint signature of the tower

In the generic simple-critical setting, the endpoint asymptotics of the tower are rigid.

The first rung \(K_1\) has opposite endpoint signs:
\[
K_1(q)\to -\infty \text{ at one end of }\mathcal I,\qquad
K_1(q)\to +\infty \text{ at the other}.
\]

Differentiating repeatedly gives the universal sign pattern:

- \(K_{2m}\) is positive near **both** endpoints;
- \(K_{2m+1}\) has opposite endpoint signs.

In particular:
\[
K_2>0 \text{ near both ends of }\mathcal I.
\]

This is a real structural fact. It means any nontrivial overlap complexity is an interior phenomenon; it is not coming from the endpoints.

That is not yet in the paper in full transport-tower language, as far as I can tell.

---

# 5. Open overlap forces a same-value / same-slope outer witness

Since \(K_1\) has opposite endpoint signs, there is at least one
\[
q_*\in\mathcal I
\]
with
\[
K_1(q_*)=0.
\]

Equivalently, if
\[
u_0:=\phi_0(q_*),\qquad u_2:=\phi_2(q_*),
\]
then
\[
\widehat Q(u_0)=\widehat Q(u_2)=q_*,
\qquad
\widehat Q'(u_0)=\widehat Q'(u_2).
\]

So the corrected overlap regime always forces a **same-value / same-slope outer witness**. This is the right transport-theoretic consequence of open overlap.

That is a theorem-level reduction and is worth recording clearly.

---

# 6. First chord-mass interpretation

Define
\[
H_1(u):=\frac{\widehat Q''(u)}{(\widehat Q'(u))^2}.
\]
Since
\[
J_1'(u)=-H_1(u),
\]
one has
\[
\boxed{
K_1(q)=
-\int_{\phi_0(q)}^{\phi_2(q)} H_1(u)\,du.
}
\]

So a witness \(K_1(q_*)=0\) is exactly a **zero-average same-value chord** for the scalar field \(H_1\).

A direct consequence is that every witness chord contains some interior point \(\xi_*\) with
\[
H_1(\xi_*)=0,
\]
equivalently
\[
\widehat Q''(\xi_*)=0,
\]
since \(\widehat Q'\neq 0\) on the outer-run interiors.

So every overlap witness brackets at least one interior inflection point.

This is already a much tighter package than “open overlap exists.”

---

# 7. Stronger Rolle package on the witness chord

The same-value / same-slope witness gives much more than one inflection point.

Let
\[
R(u):=\widehat Q(u)-\widehat Q(u_0)-p(u-u_0),
\qquad p:=\widehat Q'(u_0)=\widehat Q'(u_2).
\]
Then
\[
R(u_0)=R'(u_0)=R(u_2)=R'(u_2)=0.
\]

So \(R\) has double zeros at both endpoints. By Rolle:

- \(R''=\widehat Q''\) has at least **two** interior zeros;
- \(R'''=\widehat Q'''\) has at least **one** interior zero.

So every witness chord carries a **two-inflection / one-third-derivative** interior witness package.

This is stronger than the earlier “one inflection point” statement and is, I think, not yet reflected explicitly in the paper.

---

# 8. Correct local normal form: cubic Hermite baseline, not affine baseline

This was one of the most important corrections from my attack.

At a same-value / same-slope witness chord, the right baseline is **not** affine. It is the unique cubic Hermite interpolant matching equal endpoint values and equal endpoint slopes.

If we center the chord at
\[
m:=\frac{u_0+u_2}{2},\qquad a:=\frac{u_2-u_0}{2},\qquad y:=u-m,
\]
then the correct exact witness factorization is
\[
\boxed{
\widehat Q(m+y)
=
q_*+p\left(\frac{y^3}{2a^2}-\frac y2\right)
+
(y^2-a^2)^2\,T(y),
}
\]
for an analytic coefficient \(T\).

This replaces my earlier naive quartic factorization over an affine baseline, which was wrong.

That correction is important because it changes the interpretation of the next transport defect.

---

# 9. Exact formula for \(K_2\): thresholded endpoint asymmetry

At the witness \(q_*\), one has
\[
K_2(q_*)=\frac{\widehat Q''(u_0)-\widehat Q''(u_2)}{p^3}.
\]

Using the corrected Hermite factorization, I computed the exact endpoint formula
\[
\boxed{
K_2(q_*)
=
-\frac{6}{a\,p^2}
+
\frac{8a^2}{p^3}\bigl(T(-a)-T(a)\bigr).
}
\]

This is one of the strongest new findings.

It says \(K_2\) is **not** a pure sign invariant of the quartic remainder. It consists of:

- a universal negative cubic-Hermite baseline
  \[
  -\frac{6}{a\,p^2},
  \]
- plus an endpoint asymmetry correction from the quartic coefficient \(T\).

So \(K_2<0\) is not some mysterious transport phenomenon; it means the quartic endpoint asymmetry fails to overcome a very explicit negative baseline.

And \(K_2>0\) requires the exact threshold inequality
\[
T(-a)-T(a)>\frac{3p}{4a^3}.
\]

This is a real sharpening of the overlap lane: it becomes a **threshold asymmetry problem**.

---

# 10. Major no-go: purely local witness geometry cannot close the overlap lane

This corrected formula gives a strong negative result.

If \(T\equiv 0\), so the witness is just the cubic Hermite interpolant, then
\[
K_2(q_*)=-\frac{6}{a\,p^2}<0.
\]

So any theorem of the form:

- “local same-value / same-slope witness implies \(K_2\ge 0\),”
- “the quartic remainder alone enforces the good sign,”
- “purely local witness calculus kills overlap,”

is false.

This is one of the biggest no-gos from the whole attack.

It means the corrected overlap lane **cannot** be closed by purely local witness geometry. One needs genuinely global transport or package-level input.

That is very much in line with the current notes’ insistence that the remaining burden is transport/global/package-level, not one more local sign argument. 【180†source】【181†source】

---

# 11. Integral/moment formulas for \(K_2\)

I also derived several exact integral identities for the witness chord.

First,
\[
\boxed{
K_2(q_*)
=
-\frac1{p^3}\int_{u_0}^{u_2}\widehat Q'''(u)\,du.
}
\]

So the sign of \(K_2\) is the sign of the **total third-derivative mass** on the witness chord.

Then, with the centered coordinate \(y=u-m\), I derived:

- zero mean of \(\widehat Q''\):
  \[
  \int_{-a}^{a}\widehat Q''(m+y)\,dy=0;
  \]
- zero first moment of \(\widehat Q''\):
  \[
  \int_{-a}^{a}y\,\widehat Q''(m+y)\,dy=0;
  \]
- and the weighted identity
  \[
  \boxed{
  \int_{-a}^{a}(y^2-a^2)\,\widehat Q'''(m+y)\,dy=0.
  }
  \]

Also,
\[
\boxed{
K_2(q_*)
=
-\frac1{a^2p^3}\int_{-a}^{a}y^2\,\widehat Q'''(m+y)\,dy.
}
\]

So a bad sign \(K_2<0\) requires that \(\widehat Q'''\), despite changing sign on the chord, has the wrong signed quadratic moment about the midpoint.

This is a much tighter obstruction shape than the raw lobe-amplitude inequality.

---

# 12. Even/odd decomposition of the quartic coefficient

In the centered witness factorization
\[
\widehat Q(m+y)
=
q_*+p\left(\frac{y^3}{2a^2}-\frac y2\right)
+
(y^2-a^2)^2T(y),
\]
decompose
\[
T=T_{\mathrm{even}}+T_{\mathrm{odd}}.
\]

Then
\[
\boxed{
K_2(q_*)=-\frac{16a^2}{p^3}T_{\mathrm{odd}}(a)
-\frac{6}{a\,p^2}.
}
\]
Equivalently, the dangerous part of the quartic remainder is exactly its **midpoint-odd boundary asymmetry**, but it must also beat the universal negative cubic-Hermite baseline.

This is the clearest parity formulation I found.

It says the live overlap lane is driven by midpoint-odd asymmetry of the quartic coefficient, but only after crossing an explicit threshold.

---

# 13. Higher-rung witness escalation

The tower identity \(K_{n+1}=K_n'\) gives a very clean escalation scheme.

Since \(K_2>0\) near both ends of the overlap interval, any interior negative dip of \(K_2\) forces:

- at least two zeros of \(K_2\),
- hence at least one interior point where
  \[
  K_3=0
  \quad\text{and}\quad
  K_2<0.
  \]

So any non-monotone overlap automatically upgrades to a stronger higher-rung witness.

That is a major structural simplification:

- either \(K_2\ge 0\) and \(K_1\) is monotone, so the overlap lane reduces to a unique witness;
- or there is a higher-rung witness \(K_3=0\) with \(K_2<0\).

This is a very sharp finite witness-elimination framework and I do not think it is yet cleanly stated in the paper.

---

# 14. Best remaining theorem targets

Given all of the above, the best theorem-level targets now seem to be these.

### Target A: sign theorem for \(H_1\) on same-value outer chords
If one could prove
\[
H_1(u)=\frac{\widehat Q''(u)}{(\widehat Q'(u))^2}
\]
has one sign on every same-value outer chord, then \(K_1\) could never vanish and overlap would die immediately.

This is still the cleanest direct kill target and matches the updated note. 【181†source】

### Target B: sign theorem for \(K_2\)
Prove
\[
K_2(q)\ge 0
\]
on every genuine overlap interval.

Then \(K_1\) is monotone, so overlap reduces to exactly one same-value / same-slope witness.

### Target C: threshold asymmetry theorem
At every witness chord,
\[
T(-a)-T(a)\le \frac{3p}{4a^3}.
\]
Then \(K_2\le 0\) at every witness, which combined with endpoint positivity of \(K_2\) forces a very rigid higher-rung structure.

### Target D: package/closure law
Prove a branch-independent relation
\[
\widehat Q''=G(\widehat Q,\widehat Q')
\]
or an equivalent finite-dimensional closure law on the outer shells. Then the witness threshold asymmetry becomes a planar or finite-dimensional compatibility condition.

This is the most likely route if purely chordwise sign arguments fail.

---

# 15. Best new structural findings

The strongest findings from my whole attack, not yet stably in the draft as formal claims, are:

1. **Correct regime assignment**: the full inverse-branch / transport machinery belongs only to the overlap regime \(B_0+B_2>B_1\), not to the separation regime. 【180†source】

2. **Reciprocal-slope tower**: the overlap lane is naturally encoded by
   \[
   K_n(q)=J_n(\phi_2(q))-J_n(\phi_0(q)),
   \qquad
   K_{n+1}=K_n'.
   \]

3. **Open overlap forces a same-value / same-slope outer witness** \(K_1=0\).

4. **Every witness chord carries a strong Rolle package**: at least two interior zeros of \(\widehat Q''\) and at least one of \(\widehat Q'''\).

5. **Correct witness normal form**: the right local baseline is cubic Hermite, not affine:
   \[
   \widehat Q(m+y)=q_*+p\left(\frac{y^3}{2a^2}-\frac y2\right)+(y^2-a^2)^2T(y).
   \]

6. **Exact formula for the next defect**:
   \[
   K_2(q_*)
   =
   -\frac{6}{a\,p^2}
   +
   \frac{8a^2}{p^3}\bigl(T(-a)-T(a)\bigr).
   \]

7. **Moment formulation**:
   \[
   K_2(q_*)
   =
   -\frac1{p^3}\int_{u_0}^{u_2}\widehat Q'''(u)\,du
   =
   -\frac1{a^2p^3}\int_{-a}^{a}y^2\,\widehat Q'''(m+y)\,dy.
   \]

8. **Threshold asymmetry/no-go**: purely local witness geometry cannot close the overlap lane, because even the pure cubic Hermite witness already has \(K_2<0\). So any closure must use genuinely global transport or package-level input.

Those, to me, are the real mathematical outputs of the attack so far.

---

# 16. Strongest no-gos / negative findings

The sharpest negative results are:

- no purely local sign theorem for \(K_2\) can hold at the witness level;
- no purely quartic sign argument on the remainder \(T\) can suffice without accounting for the universal cubic baseline;
- the overlap lane is not killable by naive local contact geometry alone;
- the live obstruction, if it survives, must be genuinely transport/global/package-level.

These fit well with the current notes and should probably be reflected explicitly as ceilings if they are not already. 【180†source】【181†source】

---

# 17. Final status

So where do I think we stand?

We do **not** yet have a rock-solid theorem killing the corrected overlap lane.

But we now have a much cleaner and more honest endgame:

- the live mixed lane is the overlap regime \(B_0+B_2>B_1\);
- it forces a same-value / same-slope witness \(K_1=0\);
- every such witness has an exact cubic-Hermite-plus-quartic factorization;
- the next defect \(K_2\) is a thresholded endpoint-asymmetry / third-derivative-moment invariant;
- purely local witness geometry cannot close the lane;
- so the remaining proof burden is genuinely global/transport/package-level.

That is the full recap of what I think is real and not yet fully in the draft.
